Paternity in Overlapping 'Iddah: Resolving a Hanafi Dispute
Resolves a contradiction within Hanafi sources on paternity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on paternity when a woman remarries during her 'iddah and distinguish the views of al-Kasani and al-Kafi, applying the concept of fasid marriage.

Core Idea
A fasid second marriage during 'iddah does not transfer paternity; the child belongs to the first husband if born within two years.

This lesson resolves an apparent contradiction within the Hanafi school regarding paternity when a woman remarries during her 'iddah and gives birth. The author of Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, Ibn Nujaym, initially notes that al-Kasani in al-Bada'i' attributes the child to the second husband. However, after consulting Kafi al-Hakim, he reaffirms his own view that the child belongs to the first husband because the second marriage is fasid. We will examine the reasoning and the four scenarios of birth timing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Dispute
Recognize that there are two contradictory Hanafi positions: one from al-Bada'i' (attributing to second husband) and one from al-Kafi (attributing to first husband). The author notes this contradiction and resolves it by favoring al-Kafi.
The dispute centers on whether the woman's remarriage implies her 'iddah ended.
2
Understand al-Kafi's Argument
Examine the text from al-Kafi: it states that if the marriage occurred during 'iddah (irrevocable divorce), the second marriage is fasid, so paternity belongs to the first husband if the child is born within two years from the first divorce and at least six months from the second marriage.
Fasid marriage produces some effects (like 'iddah) but does not establish paternity against the first husband.
3
Analyze the Four Scenarios
Work through the four birth-timing scenarios given by al-Kafi: (1) 2 years from first, 2 years from first, 6 months from second → second; (4) the original disputed case (exactly 6 months from second) falls under scenario 1 if within 2 years.
The minimum pregnancy is 6 months; maximum is 2 years in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Evaluate the Thamarah al-Khilaf
Consider the practical consequences: attributing the child to the first or second husband affects inheritance, custody, and maintenance (nafaqah). The ruling determines legal relationships.
This is not merely a theoretical dispute; it has real-world implications.
5
Conclude with Tarjih
The author (Ibn Nujaym) concludes that the view from al-Kafi is preferable because it aligns with the principle that a fasid marriage does not override the original husband's paternity rights.
The mufta bihi position is that the child belongs to the first husband in the contested scenario.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وينبغي الحاقه بالأول سيأتي في أوائل ثبوت النسب عن البدائع أنه للثاني في هذه الصورة وأن نكاح الثاني جائز لأن إقدامها على التزوج دليل انقضاء عدتها من الأول اهـ. لكن راجعت كافي الحاكم فرأيته ذكر ما يوافق بحث المؤلف وعبارته هكذا وإن تزوجت المرأة في عدتها من طلاق بائن ودخل بها زوجها فجاءت بولد لأقل من سنتين من يوم طلقها الأول ولستة أشهر أو أكثر منذ تزوجها الآخر فالولد للأول لأن نكاح الآخر كان فاسداً وإن جاءت به لأكثر من سنتين منذ طلق الأول ولأقل من ستة أشهر منذ تزوجها الآخر لم يلزم الأول ولا الآخر لأن النساء لا يلدن لأكثر من سنتين ولا يلدن لأقل من ستة أشهر، وإن جاءت به لأكثر من سنتين منذ طلقها الأول ولستة أشهر منذ تزوجها الآخر ودخل بها فهو للآخر.
His statement: (And it should be attached to the first) will come in the beginning of paternity from al-Bada’i‘ that it is for the second in this scenario, and that the second marriage is permissible because her undertaking to marry is evidence of the completion of her ‘iddah from the first. But I consulted Kafi al-Hakim and saw that he mentioned what agrees with the author’s research, and his wording is as follows: If a woman married during her ‘iddah from an irrevocable divorce and her husband consummated with her, and she gave birth to a child at less than two years from the day of the first divorce and at six months or more from the second marriage, the child is for the first because the second marriage was fasid. If she gave birth at more than two years from the first divorce and less than six months from the second marriage, it does not attach to either, because women do not give birth after more than two years nor before six months. If she gave birth at more than two years from the first divorce and six months from the second marriage and consummation, it is for the second.
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hashiya-style) where the author addresses a contradiction within the Hanafi school. The author had previously stated (in the first lesson) that in the case of birth at less than two years from first divorce and exactly six months from second marriage, paternity should be assigned to the first. However, he notes that in al-Bada’i‘ (by al-Kasani), the ruling is that the child belongs to the second husband, reasoning that the woman’s action of marrying indicates her ‘iddah had ended. The author then checked al-Kafi by al-Hakim al-Shahid and found a statement that supports his own view: if the marriage was during an irrevocable divorce, the second marriage is fasid, and the child belongs to the first if born within two years. The Kafi text also clarifies the four scenarios: (1) birth 2 years from first, 2 years from first, 6 months from second → to second. Thus the author resolves the dispute by siding with al-Kafi, which aligns with his earlier ruling.

Key Terms
فاسد (fasid): A defective marriage contract that is invalid in essence but can produce some legal effects like 'iddah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Kafi, if a woman marries during her 'iddah (irrevocable divorce) and gives birth after 2 years from first divorce and 6 months from second marriage, to whom is the child attributed?
A) The first husband
B) The second husband
C) Neither husband
D) Depends on the woman's testimony

Key Takeaway
In disputed paternity cases during overlapping 'iddah, the Hanafi mufta bihi is that a fasid second marriage does not transfer paternity; the child belongs to the first husband if born within two years from the first divorce and at least six months from the second marriage.

The Beginning of 'Iddah: From the Event, Not Knowledge
Primary ruling on when 'iddah begins

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that 'iddah begins from the time of divorce or death regardless of knowledge, and explain the proof from al-Hidayah.

Core Idea
The 'iddah begins at the moment of divorce or death, whether the woman knows or not – the cause triggers the obligation.

When does a woman's waiting period start? The Hanafi school has a clear rule: the 'iddah begins from the actual event of divorce or death, not from when she finds out. This lesson unpacks the proof from al-Hidayah and how later scholars refined the distinction between cause and condition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling from the matn
The text states that the beginning of 'iddah is from the time of divorce or death, whether the woman knew or not. Even if she remains unaware and the period passes, the 'iddah is considered fulfilled.
This is the default Hanafi position from al-Hidayah.
2
Locate the dalil from al-Hidayah
The proof is that the cause (sabab) of 'iddah is the divorce or death itself. Therefore, the beginning is from the existence of the cause, not from knowledge.
The same reasoning applies to both divorce and death.
3
Understand the distinction between sabab and shart
Some texts (like Fath al-Qadir) treat marriage as the cause and separation as a condition. Al-Hidayah simplifies by calling divorce/death the cause. Later commentators reconcile by stating that divorce/death perfects the cause, making the 'iddah follow immediately.
This terminological nuance affects the conceptual understanding but not the ruling.
4
Note the cross-madhhab contrast
The Shafi'i school holds that 'iddah begins from knowledge because it is a right of the woman that only applies once she knows. The Hanafi view relies on the objective occurrence of the cause.
This difference has practical implications for cases where news is delayed.

العدة بعد الطلاق والموت وفي النكاح الفاسد بعد التفريق أو العزم على ترك وطئها ولو بشبهة ثانياً والمعتدة عن فاسد لو وطئت بشبهة للأول لكن ذكر في القنية خلافاً في الثانية . قوله : ( ومبدأ العدة بعد الطلاق والموت يعني ابتداء عدة الطلاق من وقته وابتداء عدة الوفاة من وقتها سواء علمت بالطلاق والموت أو لم تعلم حتى لو لم تعلم ومضت مدة العدة فقد انقضت لأن سبب وجوبها الطلاق أو الوفاة فيعتبر ابتداؤها من وقت وجود السبب؛ كذا في الهداية. وشرح عليه في العناية وغاية البيان والمعراج من غير تعقيب وهذا صريح فيما نقلناه عن البدائع من بيان سببها مخالف لما في فتح القدير من أن الفرقة شرطها والنكاح سببها. وقوله هنا إن في عبارة الهداية تساهلاً فقد قدموا أن سببها النكاح والطلاق شرط وأن الإضافة في قولنا عدة الطلاق إلى الشرط فالأولى أن يقال لأن عند الطلاق والموت يتم السبب فيستعقبهما من غير فصل فيكون مبدأ العدة من غير فصل بالضرورة. وذكر الشارح الزيلعي كما في فتح القدير فقال : وجعل صاحب الهداية السبب إنما هو الطلاق أو الموت وهو تجوز لكونه معملاً للعلة .اهـ. وفي الكافي شرح الوافي وقال صاحب الهداية: سبب وجوبها الطلاق أو الموت وقد نص في الأسرار أن سبب وجوبها نكاح متأكد بالدخول أو ما يقوم مقامه مما يكمل المهر عند ثبوت ما يوجب الفرقة لا الفرقة فإنها شرط اهـ. وقدمنا أن ابتداء العدة في الطلاق المبهم من وقت البيان يعني لكونه إنشاء من وجه. وفي الكافي للحاكم وغاية البيان : إذا أتاها خبر موت زوجها وشكت في وقت الموت تعتد من الوقت الذي تستيقن فيه بموته لأن العدة يؤخذ فيها بالاحتياط وذلك في العمل بيقين اهـ. وظاهر كلام محمد في المبسوط كالمختصر أن العدة تعتبر من وقت الطلاق في إقراره بالطلاق من زمان مضى إلا أن المتأخرين اختاروا وجوب العدة من وقت الإقرار حتى لا يحل له التزوج بأختها وأربع سواها زجراً له حيث كتم طلاقها ولكن لا نفقة لها ولا كسوة إن صدقته في الإسناد لأن قولها مقبول على نفسها. وفي الهداية : ومشايخنا يفتون في الطلاق أن ابتداءها من وقت الإقرار نفياً لتهمة المواضعة .اهـ. وهو المختار كما في الفتاوى الصغرى. وفي غاية البيان : أراد بالمشايخ علماء بخارى وسمرقند لا جماعة التصوف الذين هم أهل البدعة اهـ. وهو عجيب منه. والحاصل أنها إن كذبته في الإسناد أو قالت لا أدري فمن وقت الإقرار، وإن صدقته قوله : (وقدمنا إن ابتداء العدة في الطلاق المبهم أي فيما إذا قال لزوجتيه إحداكما طالق وقدمها تحت قوله ولزوجة الفار قوله : (وأما حكم وطئها في هذه المدة الخ) لينظر هل يتكرر المهر بتكرر الوطء وتقدم في باب المهر أن الأصل أن الوطء متى حصل عقب شبهة الملك مراراً لم يجب إلا مهر واحد لأن الثاني صادف ملكه كالوطء في النكاح الفاسد، وكما لو وطىء جارية ابنه أو جارية مكاتبه أو وطىء منكوحته ثم بان أنه حلف بطلاقها، ومتى حصل الوطء عقيب شبهة الاشتباه مراراً
The 'iddah after divorce and death, and in fasid marriage after separation or resolution to abandon intercourse, even if due to shubha a second time. And the woman in 'iddah from a fasid marriage, if she is subject to intercourse under shubha, the 'iddah is for the first, but there is a difference mentioned in al-Qunyah regarding the second. His statement: (And the beginning of 'iddah is after divorce and death) means the beginning of the 'iddah of divorce is from its time, and the beginning of the 'iddah of death is from its time, whether she knew of the divorce/death or did not know, even if she did not know and the period of 'iddah passed, it has expired because the cause of its obligation is the divorce or death, so its beginning is considered from the time of the cause's existence; thus in al-Hidayah. And it was explained in al-‘Inayah, Ghayat al-Bayan, and al-Mi‘raj without comment. This is explicit in what we transmitted from al-Bada’i‘ regarding the explanation of its cause, contrary to what is in Fath al-Qadir that separation is its condition and marriage is its cause. And his statement here that in al-Hidayah's expression there is leniency: they advanced that its cause is marriage and divorce is a condition, and that the addition in our expression 'iddah of divorce indicates the condition, so it is better to say because at the time of divorce and death the cause is perfected, so it follows them without separation, thus the beginning of 'iddah is by necessity without separation. And the commentator al-Zayla‘i mentioned as in Fath al-Qadir saying: The author of al-Hidayah made the cause only divorce or death, and that is a metaphor because it is used as the 'illa. (End quote) And in al-Kafi Sharh al-Wafi, the author of al-Hidayah said: The cause of its obligation is divorce or death, and it is stated in al-Asrar that the cause of its obligation is a marriage affirmed by consummation or what stands in its place that completes the mahr upon establishing what necessitates separation, not separation itself, for it is a condition. (End quote) And we have stated that the beginning of 'iddah in an ambiguous divorce is from the time of clarification, meaning because it is a type of revocation. And in al-Kafi by al-Hakim and Ghayat al-Bayan: If news of her husband's death reaches her and she doubts the time of death, she performs 'iddah from the time she is certain of his death because 'iddah is based on precaution, and that is in acting with certainty. (End quote) And the apparent meaning of Muhammad's statement in al-Mabsut and al-Mukhtasar is that the 'iddah is considered from the time of divorce when he acknowledges a divorce from a past time, except that the later scholars chose the obligation of 'iddah from the time of acknowledgment so that it is not permissible for him to marry her sister or four others as a deterrent because he concealed his divorce, but she has no nafaqah or clothing if she confirms his attribution, because her statement is accepted against herself. And in al-Hidayah: Our scholars issue fatwa in divorce that its beginning is from the time of acknowledgment to negate the suspicion of collusion. (End quote) And it is the chosen view as in al-Fatawa al-Sughra. And in Ghayat al-Bayan: He meant by 'scholars' the scholars of Bukhara and Samarkand, not the Sufi circles who are people of innovation. (End quote) And this is strange from him. The conclusion is that if she denies his attribution or says 'I don't know', it is from the time of acknowledgment; if she confirms him... his statement: (And we have stated that the beginning of 'iddah in ambiguous divorce) meaning when he says to his two wives 'one of you is divorced' and he presents it under his statement: 'And for the wife of the mouse' his statement: (And as for the ruling on intercourse during this period...) to consider whether the mahr is repeated by repeated intercourse, and it is stated in the chapter on mahr that the principle is that whenever intercourse occurs under a claim of ownership multiple times, only one mahr is obligatory because the second instance finds his ownership, like intercourse in a fasid marriage, and as if he has intercourse with his son's slave girl or his mukatab's slave girl, or if he has intercourse with his wife and then it becomes apparent that he had sworn to divorce her, and whenever intercourse occurs under a claim of confusion multiple times...
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra’iq discusses the beginning (mabda') of the 'iddah period. The primary ruling from al-Hidayah is that the 'iddah begins at the moment of divorce or death itself, regardless of the woman's knowledge. The author notes that this view from al-Hidayah is explicit in al-Bada’i‘, but contrary to Fath al-Qadir which says the cause is marriage and separation is only a condition. The author reconciles by stating that the cause is marriage, but divorce/death perfects the cause, so the beginning is from that time. He then discusses special cases: For an ambiguous divorce (e.g., saying 'one of you is divorced'), the 'iddah begins from the time of clarification. For a missing husband whose death is uncertain, she must wait until she is certain. For a man who acknowledges a past divorce, later scholars rule that the 'iddah begins from the time of his acknowledgment to prevent collusion, though the earlier view from Imam Muhammad was from the time of divorce itself. The passage also touches on the issue of whether multiple acts of intercourse under a claim of ownership (shubhat al-milk) require multiple mahr payments; the principle is that only one mahr is due because the second encounter still falls under the same claim of ownership. This is analogous to intercourse in a fasid marriage.

Key Terms
مبدأ العدة (mabda' al-'iddah): The point in time from which the 'iddah period is calculated.
سبب (sabab): Legal cause – the event that triggers the obligation of 'iddah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Hidayah, when does the 'iddah begin for a woman whose husband dies but she does not learn of his death until a year later?
A) From the time she learns of his death
B) From the time of her husband's death
C) From the time she is certain of the date
D) It does not begin until she starts mourning

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the 'iddah period begins at the moment of divorce or death, not from when the woman gains knowledge, because the cause of the obligation is the event itself.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
10 min
Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf: 'Iddah from Acknowledgment of a Past Divorce
Intra-Hanafi dispute on acknowledgment of past divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between the earlier and later Hanafi views on when 'iddah begins when a man acknowledges a divorce from a past time, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
When a man admits a past divorce, later Hanafi scholars start the 'iddah from his acknowledgment to prevent collusion, not from the alleged past date.

What happens if a man claims he divorced his wife a year ago but never told her? The earlier view from Imam Muhammad said the 'iddah began at the past date, but later scholars changed the ruling to begin from the time of acknowledgment. This lesson explores the reasoning and the final adopted position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The husband acknowledges a divorce that he claims occurred in the past (e.g., 'I divorced you one year ago'). The wife may or may not confirm this.
This is distinct from a divorce pronounced now – here the timing is contested.
2
State the earlier view (Imam Muhammad)
In al-Mabsut and al-Mukhtasar, the 'iddah is considered from the time of the claimed divorce, because the cause is the divorce itself.
This follows the general rule that 'iddah begins from the event.
3
Explain the later view and its reasoning
Later scholars (from Bukhara and Samarkand) said the 'iddah begins from the time of acknowledgment, to prevent the husband from colluding (e.g., to harm the wife by claiming a past divorce and marrying her sister).
This is an application of istihsan (juristic preference) to block potential fraud.
4
Identify the mufta bihi
According to al-Hidayah, al-Fatawa al-Sughra, and later fatwa collections, the preferred view is from the time of acknowledgment. This is the operative ruling for fatwa.
The wife's confirmations affect maintenance (nafaqah) but not the start of 'iddah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra’iq discusses the beginning (mabda') of the 'iddah period. The primary ruling from al-Hidayah is that the 'iddah begins at the moment of divorce or death itself, regardless of the woman's knowledge. مواضعة (muwada'ah): Collusion or conspiracy between spouses to deceive others.

The Cause of 'Iddah: Marriage or Divorce?
Commentary on 'iddah beginning and its cause

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two intra-Hanafi views on the cause of 'iddah and explain why the ruling on its beginning remains the same despite the theoretical difference.

Core Idea
The cause of 'iddah is debated—marriage or divorce—but the beginning is always from the event itself.

The Hanafi school agrees that a woman's 'iddah (waiting period) begins immediately upon divorce or death, even if she is unaware. However, there is a subtle theoretical debate: what is the actual cause (sabab) that necessitates the 'iddah? Is it the divorce/death itself, or is it the marriage bond that is only triggered by divorce? This lesson unpacks that dispute, showing how the same practical ruling can arise from different usul premises.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The contested point is the identification of the sabab (cause) of the 'iddah. Is it divorce/death or the marriage contract?
2
State the two views
View 1 (al-Hidayah): The cause is divorce or death. View 2 (Fath al-Qadir, al-Asrar): The cause is marriage; divorce is only a condition (shart).
3
Analyze the linguistic argument
The phrase 'iddat al-talaq grammatically adds 'iddah to talaq (divorce). View 2 argues that the idafah is to the condition, not the cause.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
There is no practical difference in the ruling: the 'iddah always begins at the moment of divorce/death. The dispute is purely theoretical.
5
Summarize the tarjih
The commentator (Ibn Nujaym) leans toward the view that marriage is the cause, but confirms that the beginning is from divorce/death.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العدة بعد الطلاق والموت وفي النكاح الفاسد بعد التفريق أو العزم على ترك وطئها ولو بشبهة ثانياً والمعتدة عن فاسد لو وطئت بشبهة للأول لكن ذكر في القنية خلافاً في الثانية . قوله : ( ومبدأ العدة بعد الطلاق والموت يعني ابتداء عدة الطلاق من وقته وابتداء عدة الوفاة من وقتها سواء علمت بالطلاق والموت أو لم تعلم حتى لو لم تعلم ومضت مدة العدة فقد انقضت لأن سبب وجوبها الطلاق أو الوفاة فيعتبر ابتداؤها من وقت وجود السبب؛ كذا في الهداية. وشرح عليه في العناية وغاية البيان والمعراج من غير تعقيب وهذا صريح فيما نقلناه عن البدائع من بيان سببها مخالف لما في فتح القدير من أن الفرقة شرطها والنكاح سببها. وقوله هنا إن في عبارة الهداية تساهلاً فقد قدموا أن سببها النكاح والطلاق شرط وأن الإضافة في قولنا عدة الطلاق إلى الشرط فالأولى أن يقال لأن عند الطلاق والموت يتم السبب فيستعقبهما من غير فصل فيكون مبدأ العدة من غير فصل بالضرورة. وذكر الشارح الزيلعي كما في فتح القدير فقال : وجعل صاحب الهداية السبب إنما هو الطلاق أو الموت وهو تجوز لكونه معملاً للعلة .اهـ. وفي الكافي شرح الوافي وقال صاحب الهداية: سبب وجوبها الطلاق أو الموت وقد نص في الأسرار أن سبب وجوبها نكاح متأكد بالدخول أو ما يقوم مقامه مما يكمل المهر عند ثبوت ما يوجب الفرقة لا الفرقة فإنها شرط اهـ.
The 'iddah occurs after divorce and death, and in an invalid marriage after separation or resolution to abandon intercourse, even if by a second shubha. And the woman in 'iddah from an invalid marriage, if she is revested by shubha, [the ruling] is for the first, but al-Qunyah mentions a difference regarding the second. His saying: (And the beginning of the 'iddah after divorce and death) means the beginning of the 'iddah of divorce is from its time, and the beginning of the 'iddah of death is from its time, whether she knows of the divorce and death or does not know, so that if she does not know and the period of 'iddah passes, it has expired, because the cause of its obligation is divorce or death, so its beginning is considered from the time of the existence of the cause; thus in al-Hidayah. And it was explained in al-'Inayah, Ghayat al-Bayan, and al-Mi'raj without commentary, and this is explicit in what we narrated from al-Bada'i' regarding the explanation of its cause, contrary to what is in Fath al-Qadir: that separation is its condition and marriage is its cause. And his statement here that there is laxity in the wording of al-Hidayah, for they have declared that its cause is marriage and divorce is the condition, and that the idafah in our saying 'iddat al-talaq is to the condition, so it is better to say: because at the time of divorce and death the cause is completed, and it follows them without interval, so the beginning of the 'iddah is necessarily without interval. And the commentator al-Zayla'i mentioned, as in Fath al-Qadir, and said: The author of al-Hidayah made the cause divorce or death, which is a metaphor because it is operative for the cause. In al-Kafi sharh al-Wafi, the author of al-Hidayah said: The cause of its obligation is divorce or death, and it is stated in al-Asrar that the cause of its obligation is a marriage confirmed by intercourse or what stands in its place that completes the dowry when something necessitating separation is established, not the separation itself, for it is a condition.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the cause (sabab) of the 'iddah. The base matn from Kanz al-Daqa'iq states that the 'iddah begins from the time of divorce or death, whether the woman knows or not. The commentator clarifies that the 'iddah begins from the event itself, and if time passes unknowingly, the 'iddah still expires because the cause is the occurrence of divorce or death. He then cites al-Hidayah, which says the cause is divorce or death, but notes that Fath al-Qadir holds a different view: that the cause is the marriage itself, and divorce is merely a condition (shart) that triggers the 'iddah. The commentator reconciles by saying that the phrase 'iddat al-talaq (the 'iddah of divorce) grammatically adds 'iddah to the condition (divorce), but the actual cause is the marriage, and divorce completes the cause. He quotes al-Zayla'i and al-Asrar to show that the majority of Hanafi scholars consider the marriage as the underlying cause, while divorce or death are the operative triggers. The practical outcome is the same: the 'iddah begins immediately upon divorce or death, but the theoretical basis differs.

Key Terms
العدة (al-iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death of her husband.
السبب (al-sabab): The cause that necessitates the obligation of the 'iddah. Here, debated whether it is divorce/death or marriage.
الشرط (al-shart): A condition that triggers the operation of the cause. In the second view, divorce is a shart, not the sabab.
الإضافة (al-idafah): Grammatical construct (idafa) linking two nouns. Here, 'iddat al-talaq: the 'iddah of divorce. The second view argues the idafah is to the shart, not the sabab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the practical difference between the two intra-Hanafi views on the cause of 'iddah?
A) One view says the 'iddah begins at divorce, the other at marriage
B) One view requires the woman to be informed, the other does not
C) There is no practical difference; both agree the 'iddah begins immediately at divorce/death
D) One view applies only to valid marriages, the other to invalid marriages

Key Takeaway
The beginning of the 'iddah is immediate from divorce or death, regardless of knowledge; the theoretical cause is debated but the ruling is unanimous.

Start of 'Iddah in Ambiguous Divorce and News of Death
Rulings on 'iddah starting from clarification in ambiguous divorce and from certainty in news of death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings on when the 'iddah begins in two cases: ambiguous divorce and uncertain news of death, and apply the underlying principles of clarification and certainty.

Core Idea
The 'iddah begins only when the cause is definitively known: clarification in ambiguous divorce, certainty in death news.

The 'iddah is a waiting period that begins when a marriage ends. But what if the ending is unclear? This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses two such scenarios: when a husband divorces one of his wives without specifying, and when a woman hears of her husband's death but not the exact time. The rulings hinge on when certainty is achieved.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
Read the passage and note the two separate rulings: ambiguous divorce (al-talaq al-mubham) and news of death with uncertain timing.
These are different triggers for 'iddah: divorce vs. death.
2
Extract the ruling for each
For ambiguous divorce: 'iddah begins from the time of clarification (al-bayan). For death news: 'iddah begins from the time she becomes certain of the death (al-yaqin).
Note the key terms: bayan (clarification) and yaqin (certainty).
3
Identify the legal principle
Both rulings rely on the principle that the 'iddah starts only when the cause is definitively known. The passage explicitly says 'the 'iddah is taken with caution' (bil-ihtiyat).
Caution requires delaying the 'iddah until certainty.
4
Apply to similar scenarios
Consider: a man says 'my wife is divorced' but he has multiple wives and does not clarify. The 'iddah does not start until he clarifies. Similarly, if news of death is rumor, she waits until verified.
This prevents premature counting of 'iddah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقدمنا أن ابتداء العدة في الطلاق المبهم من وقت البيان يعني لكونه إنشاء من وجه. وفي الكافي للحاكم وغاية البيان : إذا أتاها خبر موت زوجها وشكت في وقت الموت تعتد من الوقت الذي تستيقن فيه بموته لأن العدة يؤخذ فيها بالاحتياط وذلك في العمل بيقين اهـ.
And we have already stated that the beginning of the 'iddah in ambiguous divorce is from the time of clarification, meaning because it is a new declaration from one perspective. And in al-Kafi by al-Hakim and Ghayat al-Bayan: If news of her husband's death reaches her and she is uncertain about the time of death, she observes 'iddah from the time she becomes certain of his death, because the 'iddah is taken with caution, and that is in action based on certainty.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage gives two specific rulings on the beginning of 'iddah. First, in an ambiguous divorce (e.g., saying 'one of you is divorced' without specifying), the 'iddah begins from the time the husband clarifies which wife is divorced. This is because the divorce is considered a new declaration (insha) from that moment. Second, if a woman receives news of her husband's death but is uncertain of the exact time of death, she must observe 'iddah from the time she becomes certain of his death, acting with caution. Both rulings emphasize the principle that the 'iddah begins when the cause (separating event) is definitively known.

Key Terms
الطلاق المبهم (al-talaq al-mubham): An ambiguous divorce where the husband does not specify which wife is divorced.
العدة (al-iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death of her husband before remarrying.
البيان (al-bayan): Clarification or specification, especially in ambiguous divorce.
الاحتياط (al-ihtiyat): Caution or precaution in legal matters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The 'iddah begins only when the cause is definitively known: through clarification in ambiguous divorce and certainty in news of death.

When Does 'Iddah Begin Upon Acknowledgment of Past Divorce?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on 'iddah start after acknowledgment of past divorce.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on the start of 'iddah when a husband acknowledges a past divorce and explain why the later scholars' view is mufta bihi.

Core Idea
When a husband admits divorce from a past time, the 'iddah starts from the acknowledgment, not the claimed date, to prevent collusion.

This passage addresses a practical problem: a man says 'I divorced you one month ago.' Does the 'iddah begin from the actual divorce date or from his admission? Imam Muhammad holds one view; later Hanafi scholars, to protect against fraud, adopt a different starting point. You will see how the fatwa is given and how the wife's confirmation affects mahr and maintenance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core legal question
Determine the exact scenario: a husband acknowledges a divorce that occurred in the past. The dispute is whether the 'iddah starts from that claimed date or from the time of acknowledgment.
2
State Imam Muhammad's position and the later scholars' position
Imam Muhammad (zahir al-riwayah): 'iddah from claimed divorce date. Later scholars (mufta bihi): 'iddah from time of acknowledgment.
3
Understand the rationale for the later view
The later scholars adopted their view to negate suspicion of collusion (tuhmah) and to prevent the husband from marrying the wife's sister or four others by concealing the divorce.
4
Apply the rule to different scenarios
If the wife denies or is unsure, 'iddah from acknowledgment. If she confirms, from her perspective it is from the divorce date, but from God's perspective and in external rulings it is from acknowledgment. Note the effect on mahr and maintenance.
The wife's confirmation affects her own rights (mahr, maintenance) but not the 'iddah start for others' purposes.
5
Identify the mufta bihi view
The later scholars' view is the chosen position, as stated in al-Hidayah and al-Fatawa al-Sughra. This is the operative ruling for fatwa.
Sources: al-Hidayah, al-Fatawa al-Sughra, and the text itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وظاهر كلام محمد في المبسوط كالمختصر أن العدة تعتبر من وقت الطلاق في إقراره بالطلاق من زمان مضى إلا أن المتأخرين اختاروا وجوب العدة من وقت الإقرار حتى لا يحل له التزوج بأختها وأربع سواها زجراً له حيث كتم طلاقها ولكن لا نفقة لها ولا كسوة إن صدقته في الإسناد لأن قولها مقبول على نفسها. وفي الهداية : ومشايخنا يفتون في الطلاق أن ابتداءها من وقت الإقرار نفياً لتهمة المواضعة .اهـ. وهو المختار كما في الفتاوى الصغرى. وفي غاية البيان : أراد بالمشايخ علماء بخارى وسمرقند لا جماعة التصوف الذين هم أهل البدعة اهـ. وهو عجيب منه. والحاصل أنها إن كذبته في الإسناد أو قالت لا أدري فمن وقت الإقرار، وإن صدقته فقال: ففي حقها من وقت الطلاق وفي حق الله من وقت الإقرار وأما حكم وطئها في هذه المدة في الاختيار لها أن تأخذ منه مهراً مهراً ثانياً لأنه أقر به وقد صدقته اهـ. وفي الخانية: رجل تزوج امرأة ودخل بها ثم قال كنت حلفت إن تزوجت ثيباً قط فهي طالق ثلاثاً ولم أعلم أنها ثيب يقع الطلاق بإقراره، ثم إن صدقته المرأة كان لها نصف المهر بالطلاق قبل الدخول ومهر المثل بالدخول وعليها العدة لهذا الوطء ولا نفقة لها لأنها صدقته في وقوع الطلاق قبل الدخول، وإن كذبته المرأة في اليمين فلها مهر واحد ولها النفقة والسكني لأنها تزعم أن الطلاق وقع عليها بإقراره بعد الدخول .اهـ.
And the apparent meaning of Muhammad's statement in al-Mabsut and al-Mukhtasar is that the 'iddah is considered from the time of divorce in his acknowledgment of divorce from a past time, except that the later scholars chose the obligation of 'iddah from the time of acknowledgment, so that it is not permissible for him to marry her sister or four others, as a deterrent because he concealed her divorce. But she has no maintenance or clothing if she confirms him in the attribution, because her statement is accepted against herself. In al-Hidayah: And our shaykhs give fatwa in divorce that its beginning is from the time of acknowledgment, to negate the suspicion of collusion. That is the chosen view as in al-Fatawa al-Sughra. In Ghayat al-Bayan: He meant by 'shaykhs' the scholars of Bukhara and Samarqand, not the Sufi groups who are people of innovation. That is strange from him. The conclusion: if she denies him in the attribution or says 'I do not know', then [the 'iddah is] from the time of acknowledgment; and if she confirms him, then he said: from her perspective, from the time of divorce, and from God's perspective, from the time of acknowledgment. As for the ruling on revesting her during this period, in the option for her, she may take from him a second mahr because he acknowledged it and she confirmed him. And in al-Khaniyyah: A man married a woman and had intercourse with her, then said: 'I had sworn that if I marry a virgin, she is thrice divorced, and I did not know she was a virgin.' The divorce occurs by his acknowledgment. Then if the woman confirms him, she gets half the mahr due to divorce before consummation and the mahr of the like due to consummation, and upon her is the 'iddah for this intercourse, and she has no maintenance because she confirmed him that the divorce occurred before consummation. If the woman denies his oath, she gets one mahr, and she has maintenance and housing because she claims that the divorce occurred by his acknowledgment after consummation.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage deals with a situation where a man says 'I divorced you a month ago' (acknowledging a past divorce). There is a dispute between Imam Muhammad and later Hanafi scholars. Imam Muhammad says the 'iddah is from the claimed time of divorce, but later scholars say it is from the time of acknowledgment to prevent the husband from marrying the woman's sister etc. by concealing the divorce. The text then outlines different scenarios: if the wife confirms the husband's claim (tasdiq), then from her perspective the 'iddah is from the actual divorce, but from God's perspective it is from the acknowledgment. She can take a second mahr if revested during that period. If she denies or is unsure, the 'iddah starts from the acknowledgment. The text then gives a case from al-Khaniyyah where a man revests his wife during what he claims is the 'iddah period after a past divorce. The rulings on mahr and maintenance depend on whether she confirms or denies his claim.

Key Terms
الإقرار (al-iqrar): Acknowledgment by the husband that he divorced his wife in the past.
التهمة (al-tuhmah): Suspicion of collusion (between spouses to deceive others).

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) From the time of the actual divorce a month ago
B) From the time of his acknowledgment
C) From the time the woman learns of the divorce
D) From the time he clarifies

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fatwa, to prevent collusion, the 'iddah for a past acknowledged divorce starts from the time of acknowledgment, not the claimed date.

Day of Death vs Day of Killing in 'Iddah Calculation
Short ruling on whether the day of death or killing counts in the 'iddah period

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on counting the day of death versus the day of killing in the 'iddah of death and apply it to a given scenario.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, the day of death is excluded but the day of killing is counted in the 'iddah.

This lesson examines a subtle but important detail in the calculation of the 'iddah of death. The Hanafi school distinguishes between a natural death and a violent death, affecting whether the day of the husband's passing counts toward the four months and ten days. Understanding this rule is essential for correctly determining when the 'iddah ends.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two causes of death
Identify that the ruling separates natural death (mawt) from killing (qatl). The day of death is not counted; the day of killing is counted.
The source does not give the reasoning, but the rule is based on a broader principle explained in the author's work on legal maxims.
2
Memorize the rule
Internalize: day of natural death → excluded; day of killing → included. This is a specific Hanafi position.
3
Apply to a scenario
If the husband dies naturally at any time on Monday, the 'iddah begins on Tuesday. If he is killed on Monday, the 'iddah begins on Monday itself.
The entire day is considered for counting; partial days are treated as full days for the day of killing.
4
Recognize the source's authority
The passage is from a later commentary (Al-Bahr al-Raiq) and is based on the author's own work on qawa'id. This ruling is part of the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position.
Authority weight: fatawa mutakhkhirin (later fatwa literature).
5
Consider cross-madhhab differences
Other schools may count the day of death as the first day. The thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) is that the 'iddah ends one day earlier in cases of natural death compared to killing.
This distinction is specific to Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اعلم أن يوم الموت لا يدخل تحت القضاء ويوم القتل يدخل وقد وقعت حادثة في عدة الوفاة استخرجنا حكمها من هذه القاعدة وأوضحناها في القواعد الفقهية
Then know that the day of death is not included in the [counting of the 'iddah] and the day of killing is included. And an incident occurred regarding the 'iddah of death from which we derived its ruling from this principle and clarified it in al-Qawa'id al-Fiqhiyyah.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This short passage provides a specific rule: when calculating the 'iddah of death (four months and ten days), the day on which the husband died is not counted as part of the 'iddah period. However, if the husband was killed (e.g., murdered), the day of his killing is counted. This is a procedural detail that affects the calculation of the 'iddah. The author notes that he has elaborated on this in his work on legal maxims (al-Qawa'id al-Fiqhiyyah).

Key Terms
يوم الموت (yawm al-mawt): The day the husband dies a natural death.
يوم القتل (yawm al-qatl): The day the husband is killed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The day of killing
C) Neither day
D) Both days

Key Takeaway
The day of death is excluded, and the day of killing is included in the 'iddah of death calculation.

Claim of Prior Divorce and Its Effect on Triple Talaq
Intra-Hanafi dispute on accepting a prior divorce claim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on accepting a claim of prior divorce with expired 'iddah and identify the mufta bihi (operative ruling) with its rationale.

Core Idea
A claim of prior divorce is not automatically accepted; the fatwa guards against collusion.

Imagine a man divorces his wife three times, then claims he divorced her once long ago and her 'iddah expired. If true, the recent triple divorce would not count (since she would already be a stranger). But should the court believe him? The Hanafi school has internal disagreement. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents two views and a reconciliation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
A man issues three divorces. Afterwards, he claims that before that, there had been one divorce whose 'iddah expired, so the triple divorce did not take effect.
The claim is made after the triple talaq, not before.
2
State the Two Positions
Al-Jami' holds that both spouses are believed (their word is accepted). Ali al-Bazdawi holds that both are not believed, and this is the fatwa.
If the wife denies the prior divorce, the man is not believed even according to al-Jami'.
3
Identify the Mufta Bihi and Its Rationale
The fatwa is on al-Bazdawi: both are not believed, to prevent collusion. However, if the 'iddah expiry was publicly known, the triple divorce does not occur.
Later scholars also ruled that the 'iddah runs from the time of acknowledgment (not the claimed time), but this view is criticized.
4
Understand the Role of Evidence and Reconciliation
If the prior divorce is proven by witnesses (bayyinah) without collusion, the 'iddah is from that time. Al-Sughdi reconciled the views: Imam Muhammad's ruling (believing them) applies when spouses are separated; later scholars' view (not believing) applies when they are together.
The reconciliation limits the application to cases where collusion is likely.
5
Apply the Ruling to a New Case
Given a modern scenario, decide whether the claim is accepted based on the presence of evidence and collusion indicators.
The ruling is procedural; the substance of the prior divorce must also be valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي القنية : طلقها ثلاثاً ثم قال بعده كان قبلها طلقة وانقضت عدتها فلم تقع الثلاث وصدقته في ذلك فقد ذكر في الجامع أنهما يصدقان، وذكر علي البزدوي أنهما لا يصدقان وعليه الفتوى وإن لم تصدقه لا يصدق اهـ . وفيها: طلقها ثلاثاً ويقول كنت طلقتها قبل ذلك واحدة وانقضت عدتها؛ فإن كان انقضاء العدة معلوماً عند الناس لا يقع الثلاث وإلا يقع ولو حكم عليه بوقوع الثلاث بالبينة بعد إنكاره فلو أقام بينة أني كنت طلقتها قبل ذلك طلقة بمدة مديدة لا يلتفت إليه اهـ. وفي فتح القدير : وعرف أن تقييده بالإقرار يفيد أن الطلاق المتقدم إذا ثبت بالبينة ينبغي أن العدة من وقت قامت لعدم التهمة لأن ثبوته بالبينة لا بالإقرار اهـ. وهو مقيد بما إذا كان تأخير الشهادة لعذر ، أما إذا كان لغير عذر لم تقبل الشهادة كما في القنية. وفي الخانية الفتوى على أن العدة من وقت الإقرار صدقته أو كذبته ولا يظهر أثر تصديقها إلا في إسقاط النفقة. ووفق السغدي فحمل كلام محمد على ما إذا كانا متفرقين وكلام المشايخ على ما إذا كانا مجتمعين لأن الكذب في كلامهما ظاهر وهذا هو التوفيق إن شاء الله تعالى. وفي فتح القدير : إن فتوى المتأخرين مخالفة للأئمة الأربعة وجمهور الصحابة والتابعين رضي الله عنهم فينبغي أن يقيد بمحل التهمة ولذا قيده السغدي بأن يكونا مجتمعين.
In al-Qunyah: He divorced her three times, then afterwards said: 'There was a divorce before that and its 'iddah expired, so the triple divorce did not occur,' and she confirmed him in that. It is mentioned in al-Jami' that both are believed. Ali al-Bazdawi mentioned that both are not believed, and upon that is the fatwa. And if she does not confirm him, he is not believed. And in it: He divorced her three times and says: 'I had divorced her once before that and its 'iddah expired.' If the expiry of the 'iddah is known among the people, the triple divorce does not occur; otherwise, it occurs. And if a ruling was made against him that the triple divorce occurred based on evidence after his denial, and then he brings evidence that I had divorced her one divorce a long time before, it is not considered. In Fath al-Qadir: And it is known that his restriction to acknowledgment indicates that if the prior divorce is established by evidence, the 'iddah should be from the time it was established, due to absence of collusion, because it is proven by evidence not by acknowledgment. This is conditional on the delay of testimony being for an excuse; if for no excuse, the testimony is not accepted, as in al-Qunyah. In al-Khaniyyah, the fatwa is that the 'iddah is from the time of acknowledgment, whether she affirms him or denies him, and the effect of her affirmation only appears in the dropping of maintenance. And al-Sughdi reconciled by interpreting Muhammad's statement as when they are separated, and the shaykhs' statement as when they are together, because the lie in their speech is apparent. This is the reconciliation, if Allah wills. In Fath al-Qadir: Indeed, the fatwa of the later scholars contradicts the four Imams and the majority of the Companions and Followers, so it should be restricted to cases of collusion, and thus al-Sughdi restricted it to when they are together.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage discusses a scenario where a man divorces his wife three times, but then claims that before that, he had already divorced her once and that 'iddah had expired, so the triple divorce should not take effect (since the third divorce would be the third in a single term, but a prior divorce with expired 'iddah means the wife is a stranger, so later divorces might be invalid). There is a dispute: al-Jami' says both are believed (the man and wife), but Ali al-Bazdawi says they are not believed, and that is the fatwa. If the wife does not confirm, the man is not believed. Further, if the expiry of the 'iddah is publicly known, the triple divorce does not occur; otherwise, it does. If a court already ruled based on evidence, later evidence of a prior divorce is not accepted. Fath al-Qadir notes that if the prior divorce is proven by witnesses (not just acknowledgment), the 'iddah would be from that time, but the testimony must not be delayed without excuse. Al-Sughdi reconciles the differing views: Imam Muhammad's ruling (that 'iddah from claimed time) applies when the spouses are separated (so collusion is unlikely), while the later scholars' view (from acknowledgment) applies when they are together (collusion possible). Fath al-Qadir criticizes the later scholars' view as contradicting earlier authorities, implying it should be restricted to cases of collusion.

Key Terms
انقضاء العدة (inqida' al-iddah): The completion of the 'iddah period.
البينة (al-bayyinah): Legal evidence, typically two male witnesses.
التهمة (al-tuhmah): Collusion or suspicion of dishonesty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the fatwa (Ali al-Bazdawi), if a man divorces his wife three times and then claims a prior divorce with expired 'iddah, are he and his wife believed?
A) Yes, both are believed
B) No, both are not believed
C) Only the man is believed
D) Only the woman is believed

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi fatwa does not accept a claim of prior divorce without evidence or public knowledge, to prevent collusion between spouses.

Acting on Trustworthy News: 'Iddah and Remarriage
Ruling on 'iddah and remarriage based on trustworthy news

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a woman acting upon news from a trustworthy source regarding her husband's death or divorce, and identify the conditions under which it is permissible.

Core Idea
A woman may act upon a trustworthy person's news of her husband's death or divorce if her strongest opinion confirms it.

In Hanafi fiqh, matters of personal status like 'iddah and remarriage require careful consideration. But what if a woman cannot be absolutely certain of her husband's death or divorce? This passage from al-Jawhara provides guidance: she may rely on a trustworthy person's report if her dominant belief (akbar ra'yiha) deems it true. Let us examine the ruling and its conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a woman observing 'iddah and remarrying after being informed of her husband's death or divorce. The ruling is that it is permissible (mubah) under certain conditions.
The ruling does not make it obligatory, only allowed.
2
List the conditions for permissibility
The passage mentions two conditions: (1) the informant must be a trustworthy person (thiqa), and (2) the woman's strongest opinion (akbar ra'yiha) must be that the news is true.
The trustworthiness of the source and the woman's own conviction are key.
3
Consider the scenarios
The text covers two scenarios: a trustworthy person informing her directly, or a letter from her husband delivered by a trustworthy person. In both cases, her dominant belief suffices.
The letter scenario implies she may not recognize the handwriting, but her overall impression matters.
4
Apply the parallel case
Similarly, if a woman tells a man that she is divorced and her 'iddah has ended, he may marry her. Her statement is accepted regarding her own status.
This extends the principle to a woman's own word about her marital status.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الجوهرة: ولو أن امرأة أخبرها ثقة أن زوجها الغائب مات أو طلقها ثلاثاً أو أتاها كتاب من زوجها على يد ثقة بالطلاق ولا تدري أنه كتابه أم لا إلا أن أكبر رأيها أنه حق فلا بأس أن تعتد وتتزوج، وكذا لو قالت امرأة لرجل طلقني زوجي وانقضت عدتي لا بأس أن يتزوجها اهـ.
In al-Jawhara: If a woman is informed by a trustworthy person that her absent husband has died or divorced her three times, or a letter comes to her from her husband via a trustworthy person about divorce, and she does not know whether it is his letter or not, but her strongest opinion is that it is true, then there is no harm in her observing 'iddah and marrying. Similarly, if a woman says to a man: 'My husband divorced me and my 'iddah has expired,' there is no harm in him marrying her.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage gives a ruling on the permissibility of a woman acting upon information from a trustworthy source regarding her husband's death or divorce. If a trustworthy person (thiqa) tells her that her husband died or divorced her three times, or she receives a letter from her husband via a trustworthy person, and her dominant opinion (akbar ra'yi) is that it is true, she may observe the 'iddah and then remarry. This is based on the principle that one may act upon strong probability in such matters. Similarly, if a woman tells a man that she is divorced and her 'iddah has ended, he may marry her without further verification, as her statement is accepted regarding her own status.

Key Terms
الثقة (al-thiqah): A trustworthy person whose word is reliable in such matters.
أكبر رأيها (akbar ra'yiha): Her strongest opinion or preponderant belief.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Yes, if her strongest opinion is that it is true
C) Only if she sees the dead body
D) Only if the news comes from a court

Key Takeaway
A woman may observe 'iddah and remarry based on a trustworthy person's report if her dominant belief affirms its truth.

Multiple Intercourses during 'Iddah with Shubha and Mahr
Ruling on whether multiple revests during 'iddah with shubha require multiple mahr payments

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the default Hanafi ruling on mahr for multiple revests with shubha and identify the exception when only one mahr is due.

Core Idea
Multiple revests with shubha each require a separate mahr, unless the man was genuinely ignorant of the divorce itself.

In Hanafi fiqh, when a man claims shubha (a mistaken belief of lawfulness) and repeatedly has intercourse with a woman in 'iddah from triple divorce, the question arises: does each act require its own mahr? The default ruling, based on analogy, says yes. However, a nuanced exception appears in al-Khulasah. This lesson unpacks that ruling and its proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling
From al-Dhakhirah: each act of intercourse with shubha requires a separate mahr. Recognize this as the general principle.
The analogy is to a son's intercourse with his father's slave-girl.
2
Understand the qiyas analogy
Trace the illa: each intercourse 'meets the property of another' – i.e., violates the husband's right over the woman's reproductive capacity. This illa applies to multiple acts, hence multiple mahr.
The qiyas is jaliy (obvious).
3
Note the exception from al-Khulasah
If the three divorces were pronounced together and the man thought they did not occur, his shubha is about the cause. Then all acts are considered one transaction, and only one mahr is due.
Exception only when the mistake is about the occurrence of divorce, not its effect.
4
Apply the distinction
Determine which type of shubha applies: if the man knew the divorces occurred but thought revest was permissible, multiple mahr; if he genuinely believed no divorce occurred, one mahr.
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is multiple mahr unless the divorce ignorance is proven.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الذخيرة: فإنه يجب بكل وطء مهر على حدة لأن كل وطء صادف ملك الغير كوطء الابن جارية أبيه أو أمه او جارية امرأته مراراً وقد ادعى الشبهة فعليه لكل وطء مهر ثم قال : وفي الخلاصة لو وطىء المعتدة عن طلاق ثلاث وادعى الشبهة يلزمه مهر واحد أم بكل وطء مهر ؟ قيل : إن كانت الطلقات الثلاث جملة فظن أنها لم تقع فهو ظن في موضعه فيلزمه مهر ،واحد وإن ظن أنها تقع لكن ظن أن وطأها
In al-Dhakhirah: Indeed, for each act of intercourse, a separate mahr is obligatory, because each intercourse meets the property of another, like the intercourse of a son with his father's slave-girl or his mother's, or his wife's slave-girl repeatedly, and he claimed shubha, so for each intercourse a mahr is due. Then he said: In al-Khulasah: If one revests a woman in 'iddah from triple divorce and claims shubha, is a single mahr obligatory or a mahr for each act? It is said: If the three divorces were given together and he thought they did not occur, then his thought is in its place, and a single mahr is due. If he thought they occurred but he thought that revesting her is...
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage discusses the mahr due when a man, claiming shubha (i.e., he mistakenly thought the intercourse was lawful), has intercourse multiple times with a woman who is in 'iddah from triple divorce. The default ruling from al-Dhakhirah is that for each act of intercourse, a separate mahr is required, because each act is a transgression against the 'property' of the husband (i.e., the right of the husband over the woman's reproductive capacity). The analogy is drawn to a son having intercourse repeatedly with his father's or mother's slave-girl while claiming shubha: each act requires a separate mahr. However, al-Khulasah presents a nuance: if the three divorces were pronounced together and the man honestly thought they did not take effect, then his mistake is understandable, and only one mahr is due for all acts. If he knew the divorces occurred but thought revesting her was permissible (due to some misunderstanding), the ruling might differ. The text cuts off, but the principle is that multiple mahr are generally required unless the man's ignorance is about the occurrence of divorce itself.

Key Terms
شبهة (shubhah)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Dhakhirah, if a man revests a woman in 'iddah multiple times with shubha, how many mahr are due?
A) One mahr for all acts
B) A separate mahr for each act
C) No mahr if he claims shubha
D) Only one mahr if the woman was unaware

Key Takeaway
The default Hanafi rule is a separate mahr for each revest with shubha, but a genuine mistake about the divorce itself reduces it to a single mahr.

Ruling on Divorce When Husband Confesses Prior Oath
Ruling on divorce, mahr, and iddah when husband confesses to a conditional oath

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the effect of a husband's confession of a conditional oath on the validity of divorce and the wife's financial rights in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The husband's confession triggers divorce; the wife's response determines her financial rights.

This lesson examines a nuanced scenario from al-Khaniyyah: a husband marries and consummates, then confesses he had sworn a conditional oath that if he ever marries a thayyib, she is divorced three times, but he did not know she was thayyib. The ruling hinges on the husband's confession (iqrar) and branches based on the wife's response. Understanding this case clarifies how confession affects divorce and post-divorce entitlements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and the husband's claim
The husband marries a woman who is thayyib, consummates, then confesses that he had sworn an oath: 'If I marry a thayyib, she is divorced three times,' and he did not know she was thayyib at the time of marriage.
The confession (iqrar) is legally binding against himself.
2
Determine the effect of confession on divorce
The divorce is effective by his confession alone, regardless of whether the wife confirms or denies the oath. The act of confession establishes the occurrence of the conditional divorce.
In Hanafi law, iqrar is binding evidence against the confessor.
3
Analyze the first branch: wife confirms the husband's claim
If the wife confirms that the husband did not know she was thayyib, then the divorce is considered to have occurred before consummation. She receives half the mahr (due to divorce before consummation) and mahr al-mithl (due to consummation), but no maintenance during iddah because the marriage ended before consummation.
The text says 'half the mahr by the divorce before consummation and mahr al-mithl by consummation.' She also must observe iddah for the consummated intercourse.
4
Analyze the second branch: wife denies the husband's claim
If the wife denies that the husband had such an oath, she claims the divorce fell after consummation. She receives one full mahr and also maintenance and housing during iddah, because the divorce is considered to have occurred after consummation.
The wife's denial does not invalidate the divorce; it only changes the timing assumption affecting financial rights.
5
Extract the legal principles
Key principles: iqrar is binding; the wife's response affects the categorization of the timing of divorce (before or after consummation); this timing determines mahr, maintenance, and housing.
The ruling is a fatawa mutakhkhirin position from al-Khaniyyah, consistent with Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الخانية: رجل تزوج امرأة ودخل بها ثم قال كنت حلفت إن تزوجت ثيباً قط فهي طالق ثلاثاً ولم أعلم أنها ثيب يقع الطلاق بإقراره، ثم إن صدقته المرأة كان لها نصف المهر بالطلاق قبل الدخول ومهر المثل بالدخول وعليها العدة لهذا الوطء ولا نفقة لها لأنها صدقته في وقوع الطلاق قبل الدخول، وإن كذبته المرأة في اليمين فلها مهر واحد ولها النفقة والسكني لأنها تزعم أن الطلاق وقع عليها بإقراره بعد الدخول .اهـ.
And in al-Khaniyyah: A man married a woman and consummated, then said: 'I had sworn that if I marry a thayyib at all, she is divorced three times, and I did not know she was a thayyib.' The divorce occurs by his confession. Then if the woman confirms him, she gets half the mahr by the divorce before consummation and the mahr of the like by consummation, and upon her is the iddah for this intercourse, and no maintenance for her because she confirmed him in the occurrence of the divorce before consummation. But if the woman denies his oath, she gets one mahr, and she gets maintenance and housing because she claims that the divorce fell upon her by his confession after consummation.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage from al-Khaniyyah presents a case: a man marries a woman who is thayyib (deflowered), consummates, then later confesses that he had sworn a conditional oath that if he ever marries a thayyib, she is divorced three times, but he did not know she was thayyib at the time of marriage. The divorce falls by his own confession (iqrar). The ruling then branches based on the wife's response. If she confirms his claim (that he did not know), she gets half the mahr if divorce occurred before consummation (but here consummation happened, so she gets mahr al-mithl? The text says: 'half the mahr by the divorce before consummation and mahr al-mithl by consummation' meaning she gets the appropriate mahr for each act). Also, she must observe iddah for that consummated intercourse, but no maintenance because she agreed the divorce was before consummation and thus she is not in iddah from a valid marriage that provides maintenance? Actually, the reasoning is that she confirmed the divorce occurred before consummation, so she is not entitled to maintenance during iddah because the marriage ended before consummation. If she denies his oath and claims the divorce was after consummation, then she gets one full mahr and also maintenance and housing during iddah. The difference hinges on whether the divorce is considered to have occurred before or after consummation, affecting the wife's rights.

Key Terms
ثيب (thayyib): A woman who has been deflowered by a valid marriage.
إقرار (iqrar): Confession by the husband that he had made an oath and that the divorce occurred.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Maintenance for the iddah period
B) No maintenance
C) Half maintenance
D) Full maintenance plus housing

Key Takeaway
The husband's confession of a conditional oath triggers divorce regardless of the wife's response; her confirmation or denial only affects the timing and thus her financial rights (mahr, maintenance, housing).

Triple Divorce After Claim of Prior Divorce with Expired Iddah
Ruling on whether a subsequent triple divorce falls when husband claims a prior divorce with expired iddah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a husband pronounces triple divorce but claims a prior divorce with expired iddah, and explain the role of public knowledge and judicial finality.

Core Idea
A claim of prior divorce only prevents subsequent divorces if the iddah's expiry is publicly known.

Divorce cases often involve complex claims about prior events. This passage from al-Khaniyyah addresses a scenario where a husband pronounces three divorces but then claims he had already divorced his wife once before, and her waiting period (iddah) had expired. The ruling hinges on whether that expiry is common knowledge, illustrating the Hanafi reliance on apparent evidence and judicial stability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Claim
The husband pronounces a triple divorce (ṭalāq thalāth). He then claims that prior to this, he had divorced her once and her iddah had already expired by the time of the new pronouncement.
The prior divorce would have made the wife irrevocably separated (bainūnāt) if the iddah expired, so the subsequent triple could not fall on a non-wife.
2
Determine the Condition for Non-Occurrence
The triple does not occur if the expiry of the iddah is 'known among people' (ma‘lūman ‘inda al-nās). If not known, the triple takes effect.
Public knowledge is a factual determination, not just the husband's claim or even his evidence.
3
Understand the Effect of a Judicial Ruling
If a judge had already ruled that the triple occurred based on evidence (e.g., witnesses to the pronouncement), the husband's later evidence of a prior divorce is ignored. The judicial decision stands.
This reflects the principle that judicial rulings based on apparent evidence are final and not overturned by subsequent contradictory evidence.
4
Apply the Principle to Similar Scenarios
This ruling illustrates the Hanafi method of weighing public knowledge (shuhra) over mere claims. The condition of 'public knowledge' is a form of circumstantial evidence that takes precedence.
Compare to cases where iddah expiry is documented but not widely known.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفيها: طلقها ثلاثاً ويقول كنت طلقتها قبل ذلك واحدة وانقضت عدتها؛ فإن كان انقضاء العدة معلوماً عند الناس لا يقع الثلاث وإلا يقع ولو حكم عليه بوقوع الثلاث بالبينة بعد إنكاره فلو أقام بينة أني كنت طلقتها قبل ذلك طلقة بمدة مديدة لا يلتفت إليه اهـ.
And in it (al-Khaniyyah): He divorces her three times and says, 'I had divorced her once before that and her iddah expired.' If the expiry of the iddah is known among people, the three (divorces) do not occur; otherwise they occur. And if he is ruled against with the occurrence of the three by evidence after his denial, even if he brings evidence that he had divorced her once before that a long time ago, it is not paid attention to.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage continues from al-Khaniyyah. The scenario: a man pronounces three divorces to his wife. He then claims that before this, he had divorced her once and her iddah had already expired by the time of the new pronouncement. The ruling depends on whether the expiry of the iddah is commonly known among people. If it is known, then the wife was already divorced (and thus the new three divorces do not fall on a wife who is already irrevocably separated). If the expiry is not known, the three divorces take effect. The passage also notes that if a judge ruled against the husband based on evidence that the three divorces occurred, and then the husband brings counter-evidence that he had divorced her once long before, that counter-evidence is ignored (because the ruling is based on the apparent evidence). This illustrates the principle of judicial finality and the weight of public knowledge in legal matters.

Key Terms
انقضاء العدة (inqidā' al-‘iddah): The completion of the waiting period after divorce, after which the woman is free to remarry.
معلوماً عند الناس (ma‘lūman ‘inda al-nās): Known among people; public knowledge as opposed to private claim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case from al-Khaniyyah, if a man says 'I divorced you three times' but claims that a previous single divorce had already expired its iddah, when does the triple divorce not occur?
A) When the expiry is known among people
B) When he brings evidence of the prior divorce
C) When the wife confirms his claim
D) When the judge rules against him

Key Takeaway
The triple divorce is effective unless the prior iddah's expiry is widely known, and a judge's prior ruling on the triple divorce cannot be overturned by later evidence of a prior divorce.

Mahr for Multiple Intercourse with a Woman in Iddah
Ruling on multiple mahr for repeated intercourse with a woman in iddah, with qiyas to son and slave girl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of separate mahr for each act of unlawful intercourse and evaluate the effect of shubhah in reducing liability.

Core Idea
Each unlawful act demands a separate mahr, unless a valid shubhah excuses liability to one.

This passage from al-Dhakhirah and al-Khulasah examines a recurring question: when a man has intercourse multiple times with a woman in her iddah from a triple divorce, does he owe one mahr or many? The answer hinges on the nature of his mistake (shubhah). We will trace the analogy (qiyas) on the son and his father's slave girl, and learn to distinguish between excusable and inexcusable ignorance in Hanafi law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the general rule
Recognize that the act is repeated intercourse with a woman in iddah. The general rule from al-Dhakhirah is that each act requires a separate mahr because each act violates another's right.
2
Recognize the qiyas on the son and father's slave girl
The author draws an analogy: just as a son who repeatedly has intercourse with his father's slave girl owes a separate mahr for each act, so too does a man with a woman in iddah. Identify the 'illa (effective cause): each act meets ownership of another.
The 'illa is clear (jaliyyah), making the qiyas strong.
3
Apply the shubhah distinction from al-Khulasah
The ruling is nuanced: if the man thought the triple divorce did not occur (reasonable mistake), one mahr suffices. If he knew the divorce occurred but thought intercourse was halal (unreasonable mistake), a separate mahr for each act is due.
The distinction depends on whether the claim of shubhah is 'in its place' (zann fi mawdi'ihi) or not.
4
Note the clarification from al-Maqdisi
The passage ends with a point about when the iddah period begins. Al-Maqdisi explains it is from the time the divorce is proven by evidence, not from the time evidence is presented to the judge.
This is a minor procedural point ensuring correct application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الذخيرة: فإنه يجب بكل وطء مهر على حدة لأن كل وطء صادف ملك الغير كوطء الابن جارية أبيه أو أمه او جارية امرأته مراراً وقد ادعى الشبهة فعليه لكل وطء مهر ثم قال : وفي الخلاصة لو وطىء المعتدة عن طلاق ثلاث وادعى الشبهة يلزمه مهر واحد أم بكل وطء مهر ؟ قيل : إن كانت الطلقات الثلاث جملة فظن أنها لم تقع فهو ظن في موضعه فيلزمه مهر ،واحد وإن ظن أنها تقع لكن ظن أن وطأها حلال فهو ظن في غير موضعه فيلزمه بكل وطء مهر قوله : ( وينبغي أن تعتبر العدة من وقت قامت) قال المقدسي في شرحه أقول : مراده من وقت الطلاق الذي أقيم عليه البينة لا من وقت إقامة البينة عند القاضي اهـ فليتأمل.
And in al-Dhakhirah: For each act of intercourse, a separate mahr is obligatory because each act meets ownership of another, like a son's intercourse with his father's slave girl or his mother's or his wife's slave girl repeatedly, and he claims shubhah; so for each act, a mahr is due. Then he said: In al-Khulasah, if he has intercourse with a woman in iddah from three divorces and claims shubhah, is one mahr binding or a mahr for each intercourse? It is said: If the three divorces were in one expression and he thought they did not occur, that is a thought in its place, so one mahr is binding; but if he thought they occurred but thought intercourse was lawful, that is a thought not in its place, so for each act a mahr is binding. His statement: (And it is appropriate that the iddah be considered from the time it was established) said al-Maqdisi in his commentary: I say: His intent is from the time of the divorce for which evidence was established, not from the time of establishing the evidence before the judge. So reflect.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage from al-Dhakhirah and al-Khulasah deals with a man who has intercourse multiple times with a woman who is in iddah (waiting period) from a triple divorce. The general principle is that each act of intercourse with a woman who is not his wife requires a separate mahr (dower) because each act is a new violation of another's right. This is compared to a son who has intercourse with his father's slave girl multiple times—he owes a mahr for each act. However, the ruling is nuanced by the concept of shubhah (semblance of right). If the divorces were pronounced in one sentence (e.g., 'you are divorced three times'), and the man mistakenly thought the divorce did not actually occur, his mistake is reasonable (zann fi mawdi'ihi), so only one mahr is due. If he knew the divorce occurred but thought intercourse with a woman in iddah was permissible, his mistake is unreasonable, and he owes a separate mahr for each act. The passage ends with a remark by al-Maqdisi clarifying that when the text says 'the iddah is considered from the time it was established,' it means from the time the divorce was proven by evidence, not from the time of presenting evidence to the judge.

Key Terms
شبهة (shubhah): A semblance of right that excuses the wrongdoer from full liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man has intercourse with a woman in iddah from triple divorce multiple times, when is only one mahr due?
A) When he thought the divorces did not occur at all
B) When he knew the divorces occurred but thought intercourse was halal
C) When he had no shubhah at all
D) When he performed the acts on the same day

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, each act of unlawful intercourse normally requires a separate mahr, but a valid shubhah can reduce the liability to a single mahr if the mistake was reasonable.
