Acceptance of a Woman's Statement on Iddah Expiration
Expansion of rulings on acceptance of woman's iddah statement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a woman's claim of iddah expiry is accepted in Hanafi fiqh, and apply those conditions to specific scenarios including remarriage, miscarriage, and inheritance.

Core Idea
A woman's word on iddah is accepted only when the apparent time does not contradict, or she provides a plausible explanation like miscarriage.

In Hanafi fiqh, the expiry of iddah is often established by the woman's statement, but this acceptance is conditional. This lesson explores the detailed subsidiary rulings from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, including when her word is accepted despite apparent time contradictions, how her actions (like remarriage) can serve as implicit admission, and how her claims interact with the husband's statements and inheritance. Understanding these nuances is crucial for correctly applying fiqh in family law and fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule and exception
The passage first states that if the apparent time (e.g., minimum iddah period) contradicts her claim, her word is not accepted unless she offers a plausible explanation, such as 'I miscarried a fetus with distinct features.' This establishes the default rule and the exception.
The plausible explanation must be something that could legally end iddah immediately, like delivery or miscarriage.
2
Recognize implicit admission by action
If a woman remarries after a period sufficient for iddah, her action is treated as evidence (dalil al-iqrar) that she believed her iddah had ended. She cannot later deny this, and her statement is not accepted against either husband.
This principle highlights that actions can override later verbal claims in fiqh.
3
Distinguish between husband's and wife's claims
When the husband claims she informed him of iddah expiry, his word is not automatically accepted; she must confirm or provide detail. If the time period is possible for iddah, both are believed partially: he is believed regarding his own rights (e.g., marrying her sister), she regarding her maintenance and housing.
Maintenance can be due for reasons other than iddah, so her right to it remains even if she is contradicted.
4
Analyze inheritance scenario and ikhtilaf
If the husband marries her sister and dies, inheritance is generally for the sister. There is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: if the first woman is given inheritance, does that invalidate the sister's marriage? The preferred view (al-ashah) is that it does not, because inheritance can be due from other causes.
This shows that rulings on marriage validity are not automatically affected by financial rights.
5
Examine pregnancy claim changes
A widow who first says she is not pregnant, then later says she is, is believed if the initial statement was within the period of possibility. But if she denies pregnancy after the full iddah (4 months 10 days), her later claim is not accepted unless she delivers a child within 6 months of the husband's death.
This balances the risk of false claims against protecting lineage and women's honor.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اعلم أنه إذا كذبها الظاهر بالنسبة إلى المدة لا يقبل قولها عند عدم التفسير، أما لو فسرت بأن قالت أسقطت سقطاً مستبين الخلق أو بعضه قبل قولها لأن الظاهر لا يكذبها؛ كذا البدائع. فعلم أن انقضاءها لا ينحصر في إخبارها بل يكون به وبالفعل بأن تزوجت بزوج في آخر بعدما مضت مدة تنقضي في مثلها العدة حتى لو قالت بعده لم تنقض لم تصدق لا في حق الزوج الأول ولا في حق الثاني لأن الإقدام عليه دليل الإقرار كذا في البدائع وفي فتح القدير وعكس هذه المسألة إذا قال الزوج أخبرتني بأن عدتها قد انقضت، فإن كانت في مدة تنقضي في مثلها لا يقبل قوله ولا قولها إلا أن تبين ما هو محتمل من إسقاط سقط مستبين الخلق فحينئذ يقبل قولها، ولو كان في مدة تحتمله فكذبته لم تسقط نفقتها وله أن يتزوج بأختها لأنه أمر ديني يقبل قوله فيه اهـ .
فالحاصل أنه يعمل بخبريهما بقدر الإمكان بخبره فيما هو حقه وحق الشرع وبخبرها في حقها من وجوب النفقة والسكنى ولو جاءت بولد لأكثر من ستة أشهر يثبت نسبه منه لأنه في النسب حقها أصلي كحق الولد لأنها تعير بولد ليس له أب معروف فلم يقبل قوله ولا ينفذ نكاح أختها لأنه لا يتصور استحقاق النسب إلا ببقاء الفراش فصار الزوج مكذباً في خبره شرعاً بخلاف القضاء بالنفقة لأنه يتصور استحقاق النفقة لغير العدة فكأنه وجبت في العدة حقها بسبب وفي حقه بسبب آخر، فإن تزوج أختها ومات فالميراث للأخرى؛ هكذا ذكر محمد في النكاح . وقيل ؛ إن قال هذا في الصحة ثم مات فالميراث للأخرى لا للمعتدة، وإن قال في المرض فالميراث للمعتدة فإذا قضى بالميراث للمعتدة قيل يفسد نكاح أختها والأصح أنه لا يفسد لأنه يتصور استحقاق الميراث بغير الزوجية فنزل منزلة استحقاق النفقة؛ كذا في المحيط. وفي الخانية : امرأة قالت في عدة الوفاة لست بحامل ثم من الغد قالت أنا حامل كان القول قولها وإن قالت بعد أربعة أشهر وعشرة أيام لست بحامل ثم قالت أنا حامل لا يقبل قولها إلا أن تأتي بولد لأقل من ستة أشهر من موت زوجها فيقبل قولها ويبطل إقرارها بانقضاء العدة
قوله : (وإن لم تقر بسقط لاحتماله قال في النهر : الظاهر أنه لا بد من بيانها صريحاً كما مر . وقال الرملي : قوله وإن لم تقر الخ» تقدم تضعيفه في باب الرجعة فراجعه .
Then know that if the apparent (time) contradicts her regarding the period, her statement is not accepted in the absence of explanation. But if she explained by saying 'I miscarried a stillborn with distinct creation, or part of it', her statement is accepted because the apparent does not contradict her. So it is understood that the expiry is not limited to her informatio; rather, it is also by action, such as her marrying another husband after a period in which iddah could have expired, so even if she says later 'it has not expired', she is not believed, neither in the right of the first husband nor the second, because the action (remarriage) is evidence of admission. The opposite of this issue: if the husband said, 'she informed me that her iddah has expired', then if it is in a period in which it can expire, his statement is not accepted, nor hers, unless she clarifies with something plausible like a miscarriage of a stillborn distinct creation, then her statement is accepted. And if it is in a period that admits it and he denies her, her maintenance is not dropped, and he may marry her sister, because it is a religious matter in which his statement is accepted. So the conclusion is that we act on both of their statements as much as possible: on his statement regarding what is his right and the right of the Shari'ah, and on her statement regarding her right of maintenance and housing. And if she brings a child after more than six months, his lineage is established from him, because lineage is originally her right like the child's right, since she is disgraced by having a child without a known father, so his statement is not accepted, and the marriage to her sister is not valid, because entitlement to lineage cannot be imagined except by survival of the marital bed (firash). So the husband is deemed contradicted in his information shar'i. Unlike the ruling on maintenance, because entitlement to maintenance can be imagined for reasons other than iddah, so it is as if it is wajib in iddah: her right due to one reason and his right due to another. So if he marries her sister and dies, the inheritance is for the other (the sister). That is what Muhammad mentioned in al-Nikah. And it is said: if he said this in health and then died, the inheritance is for the other, not for the woman in iddah. And if he said it in illness, the inheritance is for the woman in iddah. Then if inheritance is awarded to the woman in iddah, it is said: the marriage to her sister becomes invalid. The more correct view is that it does not become invalid, because entitlement to inheritance can be imagined through other than marriage, so it is treated like entitlement to maintenance. This is in al-Muhit. And in al-Khaniyyah: A woman in iddah of death said 'I am not pregnant', then the next day she said 'I am pregnant', her statement is accepted. And if she said after four months and ten days 'I am not pregnant', then said 'I am pregnant', her statement is not accepted unless she brings a child born less than six months from her husband's death, then her statement is accepted and her admission of iddah expiry is invalid. His saying: (And if she did not confess to a miscarriage, due to its possibility.) He said in al-Nahr: Apparently, she must state clearly, as before. And al-Ramli said: His saying 'and if she did not confess...' etc. Its weakness has been mentioned earlier in the chapter of Raj'ah, so refer to it.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage is a collection of subsidiary rulings derived from the main principle that a woman's word about her iddah is conditionally accepted. It begins by stating that if the apparent time contradicts her claim, she must provide a plausible explanation (e.g., miscarriage) to be believed. If she remarries after a period sufficient for iddah, that action itself is evidence that her iddah ended—so she cannot later deny it. Conversely, if the husband claims she informed him that her iddah ended, his word is not automatically accepted; she must confirm or provide detail. The passage then explains that both statements are harmonized: the husband's word prevails in matters of his own rights (e.g., marrying her sister), while her word prevails in matters of her maintenance and housing. If she gives birth to a child more than six months after divorce, lineage is established from him, overriding the husband's denial. The discussion continues with inheritance implications if the husband married her sister and dies—the correct view is that the first wife's inheritance does not invalidate the second marriage. Finally, a case from al-Khaniyyah about a widow who changes her claim of pregnancy is given. The closing remark from al-Ramli indicates that the issue of not confessing to miscarriage requires explicit statement.

Key Terms
سقط مستبين الخلق (suqt mustabin al-khalq): A miscarriage in which the fetus has distinct human features; this serves as evidence that iddah expired due to delivery.
دليل الإقرار (dalil al-iqrar): Action that constitutes an implicit admission; here, remarriage after possible iddah implies she believes iddah is over.
الأصح (al-ashah): The more correct view; used to denote the preferred opinion among multiple Hanafi positions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A woman's statement about iddah expiry is conditionally accepted; if the time contradicts, she must provide a plausible explanation like miscarriage, and her actions (especially remarriage) can override later claims.

Ruling on Marrying a Woman in Her Iddah and Divorcing Before Consummation
Intra-Hanafi dispute on mahr and iddah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three intra-Hanafi rulings on mahr and iddah when a man marries a woman in her iddah and divorces before consummation, and explain the Sahibayn's qiyas that leads to full mahr and a new iddah.

Core Idea
Full mahr and new iddah due to imputed possession from prior consummation.

This lesson examines a specific intra-Hanafi dispute: a man marries a woman who is currently in her iddah from a previous marriage, then divorces her before consummating the new marriage. The general rule for pre-consumption divorce is half mahr and no iddah, but here the scholars differ because the woman is already in the man's effective possession due to the first marriage's consummation and ongoing iddah. We will walk through the three positions and their proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and three views
The case: man marries his mu'taddah (woman in iddah from prior marriage) and divorces before consummation. Three views: Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani): full mahr and new iddah. Imam Muhammad: half mahr and complete first iddah. Zufar: no iddah at all.
2
Examine the Sahibayn's proof
The Sahibayn analogize to a ghassib (usurper) who buys the usurped property: the contract itself gives possession. Here, the first consummation and its remaining iddah make the woman effectively in his possession, so the new marriage is treated as post-consummation.
This is an istihsan-based qiyas.
3
Examine Muhammad and Zufar's counterproofs
Imam Muhammad applies the general rule: divorce before consummation yields half mahr and no new iddah; the first iddah continues. Zufar argues no iddah at all because the first iddah ended with the new marriage and the second never started, citing Quran 33:49.
Zufar relies on the zahir of the Quranic text.
4
Understand the tarjih
The Sahibayn's view is preferred (mufta bihi) because it preserves the purpose of iddah (preventing lineage confusion) and is supported by strong analogy. The author in Fath al-Qadir rules that Zufar's view, though an ijtihad, would nullify the wisdom of iddah.
A judge may still enforce Zufar's ruling due to legitimate ijtihad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ولو نكح معتدته وطلقها قبل الوطء وجب مهر تام وعدة مبتدأة) وهذا عندهما . وقال محمد عليه نصف المهر وعليها إتمام العدة الأولى لأنه طلاق قبل المسيس فلا يوجب كمال المهر ولا استئناف العدة، وإكمال العدة الأولى إنما وجبت بالطلاق الثاني فظهر حكمه كما لو اشترى أم ولده ثم أعتقها ولهما أنها مقبوضة في يده حقيقة بالوطأة الأولى وبقي أثره العدة فإذا جدد النكاح وهي مقبوضة ناب ذلك عن القبض المستحق في هذا النكاح كالغاصب يشتري المغصوب الذي في يده يصير قابضاً بمجرد العقد، فوضح بهذا أنه طلاق بعد الدخول. وقال زفر : لا عدة عليها أصلاً لأن الأولى قد سقطت بالتزوج فلا تعود والثانية لم تجب وجوابه ما قلناه وما قاله زفر فاسد لأنه يستلزم إبطال المقصود من شرعها وهو عدم اشتباه الأنساب ؛ كذا في فتح القدير. ومع ذلك هو مجتهد فيه صرح به في جامع الفصولين لو قضى به قاض نفذ قضاؤه لأن للاجتهاد فيه مساغاً وهو موافق الصريح القرآن ثم طلقتموهن من قبل أن تمسوهن فما لكم عليهن من عدة تعتدونها [الأحزاب: ٤٩]١ هـ قوله : (إنما وجبت بالطلاق الثاني فظهر حكمه كذا في أغلب النسخ وهو غير صحيح فالصواب ما في بعضها إنما وجبت بالطلاق الأول وبالثاني ظهر حكمه قال في الفتح : غير أن إكمال العدة الأولى وجب بالطلاق الأول لكنه لم يظهر حكمه حال التزوج الثاني، فإذا ارتفع بالطلاق ظهر حكمه قوله : (كما لو اشترى أم ولده قال في الفتح : أي زوجته التي هي أم ولده إذا كانت أمة فإنه ينفسخ النكاح بالشراء ولم تظهر العدة حتى حل وطؤها بملك اليمين ثم بالعتق تظهر غير أن هنا تجب عليها عدة أخرى لأنها أم ولد أعتقت وتداخلت العدتان فيجب عليها الإحداد إلى أن تذهب العدة،
His statement: (And if he marries his woman in iddah and divorces her before intercourse, then a full mahr is obligatory and a new iddah) — this is according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). And Muhammad said: Upon him is half the mahr, and upon her is completion of the first iddah, because it is a divorce before consummation, so it does not necessitate complete mahr nor renewal of iddah. And the completion of the first iddah was only obligated by the second divorce, so its ruling appeared, like if he bought his umm walad then freed her. And according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), that she is in his actual possession by the first intercourse, and its effect remains as iddah. So when he renews the marriage while she is in his possession, that substitutes for the possession required in this marriage, like a usurper who buys the usurped property that is in his hand: he becomes a possessor by the mere contract. Thus it is clear that this is a divorce after consummation. And Zufar said: No iddah is upon her at all, because the first has fallen by the marriage and does not return, and the second has not been obligated. His response is what we said, and what Zufar said is invalid because it necessitates nullifying the purpose of its legislation, which is avoiding confusion of lineages. So in Fath al-Qadir. And despite that, he is a mujtahid — it is stated in Jami' al-Fusulayn that if a judge ruled by it, his judgment is executed because there is scope for ijtihad, and it is in agreement with the clear text of the Qur'an: 'Then you divorced them before you touched them, so there is no iddah for you to count' [Al-Ahzab:49]. His statement: (The completion was only obligated by the second divorce, so its ruling appeared) — this is in most copies, but it is incorrect. The correct version in some copies is: 'The completion was only obligated by the first divorce, and by the second its ruling appeared.' He said in al-Fath: However, the completion of the first iddah was obligated by the first divorce, but its ruling did not appear at the time of the second marriage; so when it is raised by the divorce, its ruling appears. His statement: (like if he bought his umm walad) — he said in al-Fath: meaning his wife who is his umm walad, if she is a slave, then the marriage is dissolved by the purchase, and the iddah does not appear until her sexual use becomes permissible by right hand possession; then by emancipation it appears, except that here another iddah is obligatory upon her because she is an umm walad who was freed, and the two iddahs overlap, so she must observe ihdad until the iddah ends.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a specific case: a man marries a woman who is in her iddah (waiting period) from a previous marriage, then divorces her before consummating the new marriage. The author states the ruling according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) that a full mahr is obligatory and a new iddah begins. Muhammad al-Shaybani himself has a different opinion: only half mahr and completion of the first iddah. The reasoning is that the divorce occurred before consummation in the new marriage, so the general rule of half mahr applies. However, the Sahibayn analogize this to a ghassib (usurper) who buys the usurped property — the contract itself acts as possession. Here, the first marriage's consummation and its ongoing iddah make the woman effectively in the man's possession, so the new marriage is considered consummated from the start. Zufar argues no iddah at all because the first iddah ended with the new marriage and the second never began, but the author refutes this as undermining the purpose of iddah (avoiding lineage confusion). The passage also clarifies a textual correction in the phrase 'the completion was only obligated by the second divorce' in some manuscripts.

Key Terms
عدة (iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death before remarrying.
مهر (mahr): The bridal gift (dower) that a husband must give to his wife upon marriage.
معتدة (mu'taddah): A woman who is observing iddah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on mahr and iddah when a man marries a woman in her iddah and divorces her before consummation?
A) Half mahr and no iddah
B) Half mahr and completion of the first iddah
C) Full mahr and a new iddah
D) Full mahr and no iddah

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, marrying a woman in her iddah and divorcing before consummation requires full mahr and a new iddah, according to the mufta bihi view, because the prior consummation imputes possession to the second marriage.

Applying Prior Consummation: Conditional Talaq and Multiple Marriages
Applies prior consummation principle to conditional talaq and fasid marriage branches

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that consummation in a prior marriage during iddah is deemed consummation in subsequent marriages to calculate mahr and divorces in conditional talaq scenarios.

Core Idea
Consummation in an earlier marriage is legally imputed to later marriages during iddah.

This passage extends a foundational principle from earlier in the text: if a woman is in iddah from a prior marriage, any future marriage with the same husband is considered to have occurred after consummation, based on the first consummation. The author applies this to a clever hypothetical where a man repeatedly marries and divorces his wife in one day, leading to different mahr and divorce counts between Imam Muhammad and the Sahibayn. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to trace how a single principle yields divergent rulings in complex scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core principle
The passage begins by restating the principle: 'al-dukhul fi al-nikah al-awwal dukhul fi al-thani' — consummation in the first marriage is consummation in the second. This applies when marriages occur during the iddah from the first marriage.
This principle is from the Sahibayn and is mufta bihi.
2
Set up the conditional talaq case
A man says to his wife, 'Whenever I marry you, you are divorced.' He then marries her three times in one day, consummating each time. Determine the mahr and number of divorces under the Sahibayn and under Muhammad.
The key is whether each marriage is considered before or after consummation.
3
Trace Muhammad's calculation
Muhammad treats each marriage and consummation independently. First marriage: divorce before consummation → half mahr + one divorce. After first consummation → full mahr. Second marriage: divorce before consummation → half mahr + second divorce. After second consummation → full mahr. Third marriage: divorce + consummation → full mahr + third divorce. Total: 4.5 mahr, 3 divorces.
Muhammad does not impute the first consummation to later marriages.
4
Trace the Sahibayn's calculation
The Sahibayn impute the first consummation to all later marriages. First marriage: divorce after consummation (imputed) → full mahr + one divorce. First actual consummation → no extra mahr (already counted). Second marriage: divorce after consummation (imputed) → full mahr + second divorce. Second consummation: considered revocation (raj'ah) if revocable, so no new mahr. Third marriage: invalid because she is already married (after three divorces). Total: 2.5 mahr (or 5.5 for irrevocable variant), 2 divorces (or 3 for irrevocable).
The principle reduces overall liability and divorces.
5
Examine the fasid marriage branches
The passage also applies the principle to cases involving fasid (defective) marriages. If a valid marriage follows a fasid marriage during iddah, consummation in the fasid counts for the valid, triggering full mahr and new iddah. If reversed (valid then fasid), the fasid is ignored because actual intercourse is impossible.
The distinction hinges on whether actual intercourse is possible.

And among the most useful issues built upon this principle is that consummation in the first marriage is consummation in the second. Branching from it: If he said, 'Whenever I marry you, you are divorced,' and he married her three times in one day and consummated each time, then according to Muhammad he is liable for four and a half mahr and she is separated by three (divorces), and according to them (the Sahibayn) two divorces and two and a half mahr, or if (the divorce is) irrevocable, he is liable for those mahr — them (the Sahibayn) say five and a half: half mahr for the first divorce before consummation, two mahr for the two divorces because they are after consummation effetively, and three mahr for the three consummations. Its completion is in Sharh al-Majma' from al-Ta'liq. Then know that consummation in the first is consummation in the second regarding mahr and obligation, but regarding revocation (raj'ah) if the divorce was revocable, he does not own her, as in Fath al-Qadir. Second: If he married her with a fasid (defective) marriage and consummated, then they were separated, then he married her validly while she was in iddah from that fasid, then divorced her before consummation, then a full mahr is obligatory on him and a new iddah on her according to them. And if it were reversed — that he married her first validly, then divorced her after consummation, then married her in iddah with a fasid marriage — no mahr is obligatory on him nor a new iddah on her, and she must complete the first iddah by agreement. The distinction for them is that he is not able to have actual intercourse in the fasid marriage, so he is not considered a consummator effetively due to the impossibility in reality; likewise he is not considered a consummator by seclusion in fasid marriage, so iddah is not obligated by it nor mahr. Third: that if he consummated in a valid marriage? (incomplete) 'the iddah of marriage and it is two menses from the time of purchase.' His statement: (He is liable for four mahr) meaning Muhammad holds the husband liable. And his statement 'and she is separated' means Muhammad said she is irrevocably divorced by three. Ibn al-Malik said: This disagreement is built on what came before: that if a separated woman (mubannah) is married by her husband in her iddah and divorced before consummation, then according to him (Muhammad) she must complete the first iddah because consummation in the first marriage is not consummation in the second, and according to them (the Sahibayn) she has a new iddah because consummation in the first is consummation in the second. So Muhammad says: by the first marriage she is divorced and gets half mahr, after consummation another mahr; by the second marriage she is divorced also and gets half mahr, after the second consummation another mahr; by the third marriage and third consummation she gets one and a half mahr, totaling four and a half mahr. And the Sahibayn say: by the first marriage and consummation after it she gets one and a half mahr; by the second marriage a full mahr because this is a divorce after consummation since the first consummation is consummation in the second; and by the second consummation he becomes a revoker (muraji') and nothing is obligatory; and the third marriage is disregarded because marrying a woman who is already married in valid marriage is invalid. And his statement 'or irrevocably' means if he said, 'Whenever I marry you, you are irrevocably divorced,' and he married her three times in one day and consummated each time, then he is liable for those mahr — i.e., Muhammad said she gets four and a half mahr, analogizing to the previous issue. The Sahibayn say five and a half, and she is irrevocably divorced by three by agreement. They said: by the first marriage and consummation after it one and a half mahr; by the second marriage she is divorced a second time and gets a full mahr because it is divorce after consummation according to their principle, and another mahr after consummation for the ambiguity (shubhah), and he does not become a revoker because the divorce is irrevocable; and by the third marriage she is divorced a third time, and she gets a mahr and after consummation another mahr, totaling five and a half mahr — three mahr obligated by three consummations, half mahr for the first marriage, and two mahr for the other two marriages. End.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the principle established earlier: that consummation in an earlier marriage counts as consummation in a later marriage occurring during the iddah. The author applies this principle to several branches. The first branch is a hypothetical: a husband says to his wife, 'Whenever I marry you, you are divorced,' then he marries her three times in one day, consummating each time. The calculation of mahr and number of divorces differs between Imam Muhammad and the Sahibayn, based on whether each marriage is considered post-consummation or not. The second branch deals with fasid (defective) marriages: if a woman is married and divorced from a fasid marriage, then married validly in iddah and divorced before consummation, the Sahibayn rule full mahr and new iddah. If the order is reversed (valid then fasid), no mahr or new iddah, and she completes the first iddah. The third branch appears incomplete but addresses a case of valid marriage consummation. The passage then provides a detailed commentary by Ibn al-Malik explaining the differences in the conditional talaq case, citing the foundational disagreement between Muhammad and the Sahibayn on whether the first consummation counts in the second marriage.

Key Terms
دخول (dukhul): Sexual consummation of marriage.
بائن (bā'in): Irrevocable divorce (three divorces or khul') that eliminates the right to revoke.
رجعة (raj'ah): Revocation of a revocable divorce (talaq raj'i) during the iddah period.
فاسد (fāsid): A defective marriage that lacks some condition but can be validated (as opposed to bātil, which is void).

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Four and a half mahr
C) Five and a half mahr
D) Three mahr

Key Takeaway
The principle that consummation in an earlier marriage during iddah imputes to later marriages is a key tool in calculating mahr and divorces in sequential marriages, with the Sahibayn's view prevailing in the school.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Mahr in Conditional Divorce with Multiple Marriages
Explains the first scenario based on the principle of dukhul in first marriage counting for the second.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain and compare the Hanafi positions of Imam Muhammad and the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) regarding the mahr owed when a man says 'Whenever I marry you, you are divorced' and marries her multiple times in one day, consummating each marriage.

Core Idea
The key is whether the consummation in the first marriage legally counts as consummation in subsequent marriages.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explores a detailed intra-Hanafi dispute arising from a conditional divorce phrase. The ruling hinges on a foundational principle about the legal effect of consummation across successive marriages. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to trace how a single principle generates different results in derived cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditional phrase and scenario
The man says 'Whenever I marry you, you are divorced' and then marries her three times in one day, consummating each time. The question is: how many mahr and divorces result?
Note that the divorces occur at each marriage, but the timing of consummation affects the mahr.
2
State the two Hanafi positions
Imam Muhammad holds that each marriage is independent, resulting in 4.5 mahr and three divorces (in the raj'i case). The two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that the first consummation counts for the second marriage, resulting in 5.5 mahr and only two divorces (in the raj'i case). In the ba'in case, both agree on three divorces but differ on mahr (4.5 vs 5.5).
The difference of one mahr is the thamarah al-khilaf.
3
Identify the underlying principle
The core principle is whether the consummation (dukhul) in the first marriage is legally considered consummation in the second marriage. Muhammad says no; the two say yes.
This principle is derived from an earlier case about a separated woman who remarries in her 'iddah.
4
Link to the earlier 'iddah principle
The same disagreement applies: if a woman is divorced (ba'in) and remarries in her 'iddah, Muhammad says she completes the first 'iddah (first consummation does not count for second marriage), while the two say she starts a new 'iddah (first consummation counts).
Ibn al-Malik's commentary explicitly connects the two cases.
5
Analyze the practical difference
The difference of one mahr and the number of divorces in the raj'i case. In the ba'in case, only the mahr differs. Both positions are recorded in Zahir al-Riwayah, and the text does not give explicit tarjih, but later preference may lean toward the two.
The student should be able to compute both scenarios.

Source Text

كتاب الطلاق باب العدة العدة، وهذه أجدى المسائل المبنية على هذا الأصل وهو أن الدخول في النكاح الأول دخول في الثاني أولاً، ويتفرع عليه لو قال كلما تزوجتك فأنت طالق فتزوجها في يوم : ثلاثاً ودخل بها في كل مرة ألزمه أربعة مهور ونصف وأبانها بثلاث وحكماً بتطليقتين ومهرين ونصف أو بائناً ألزمه بتلك المهور وهما بخمسة ونصف نصف مهر بالطلاق الأول قبل الدخول ومهران بالتطليقتين لكونهما بعد الدخول حكماً وثلاث مهور بالدخول ثلاثاً وتمامه في شرح المجمع من التعليق. ثم اعلم أن الدخول في الأول دخول في الثاني في حق المهر ووجوب وأما في حق الرجعة لو كان الطلاق رجعياً لا يملكها كما في فتح القدير. قوله : (ألزمه أربعة مهور أي ألزم محمد الزوج. وقوله وأبانها» أي قال محمد بانت منه بثلاث طلقات قال ابن الملك : هذا الخلاف مبني على ما تقدم من أن المبانة إذا نكحها الزوج في عدتها وطلقها قبل الدخول بها فعليها إتمام العدة الأولى لأن الدخول في النكاح الأول ليس بدخول في الثاني عنده وعليها عدة مستقبلة عندهما لأن الدخول في الأول دخول في الثاني، فمحمد يقول بالتزوج الأول طلقت ولها نصف المهر وبالدخول بعده مهر آخر، وبالتزوج الثاني طلقت أيضاً ولها نصف مهر وبالدخول الثاني مهر أيضاً، وبالتزوج الثالث والدخول الثالث لها مهر ونصف فصار أربعة مهور ونصف مهر وهما يقولان بالتزوج الألأل والدخول بعده لها مهر ونصف مهر، وبالتزوج الثاني مهر . تام لأن هذا طلاق بعد الدخول لكون الدخول الأول دخولاً في الثاني، وبالدخول الثاني صار مراجعاً ولا يجب شيء، ولا اعتبار بالتزوج الثالث لأن نكاح المنكوحة غير صحيح. وقوله «أو بائناً» يعني لو قال كما تزوجتها فبائن فتزوجها في يوم ثلاث مراث ودخل بها في كل مرة ألزمه بتلك المهور أي قال محمد لها أربعة مهور ونصف اعتباراً بالمسألة السابقة. وهما بخمسة ونصف وبانت بثلاث اتفاقاً هما قالا : وجب لها بالنكاح الأول وبالدخول بعده مهر ونصف مهر، وبالنكاح الثاني طلقت ثانياً ولها مهر كامل لأنه طلاق بعد الدخول على أصلهما، ومهر آخر بالدخول بعده للشبهة ولم يصر به مراجعاً لأن الطلاق بائن وبالنكاح ثالثاً طلقت ثالثاً، ولها مهر وبالدخول بعده مهر آخر فصار خمسة مهور ونصف ثلاثة مهور وجبت بثلاثة دخول ونصف مهر بالنكاح الأول ومهران بالنكاحين الآخرين اهـ.
Book of Divorce, Chapter of 'Iddah. 'Iddah. And this is one of the issues based on this principle: that entering (consummation) in the first marriage is a legal entry into the second marriage in the first place. And it branches from it: if he said, 'Whenever I marry you, you are divorced,' and he married her three times in one day and consummated each time, he is obligated four and a half mahr, and Muhammad said she is separated by three, and according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) it is two divorces and two and a half mahr, or if ba'in, he is obligated those mahr and they say five and a half: half mahr for the first divorce before consummation, two mahr for the two divorces because they are after consummation in legal opinion, and three mahr for the three consummations. Then know that consummation in the first is consummation in the second regarding the mahr and obligation, but regarding the right of return (raj'ah) if the divorce was revocable, he does not own her as in Fath al-Qadir. His saying: (He obligated four mahr) meaning Muhammad obligated the husband. And his saying: 'and she is separated' meaning Muhammad said she is separated from him by three divorces. So Muhammad says: by the first marriage she is divorced and gets half mahr, and after consummation another mahr; by the second marriage she is also divorced and gets half mahr, and by the second consummation another mahr; by the third marriage and third consummation she gets one and a half mahr, total four and a half mahr. The two say: by the first marriage and consummation she gets one and a half mahr; by the second marriage a full mahr because this divorce is after consummation since the first consummation counts for the second, and by the second consummation he becomes a reverter and nothing is required; the third marriage is not considered because marrying a married woman is invalid. And his saying 'or ba'in' means if he said 'whenever I marry you, you are ba'in,' and he married her three times in one day and consummated each time, he is obligated those mahr: Muhammad said she gets four and a half mahr by analogy with the previous case. The two say five and a half, and she is separated by three unanimously. The two said: she is owed by the first marriage and consummation one and a half mahr; by the second marriage she is divorced a second time and gets a full mahr because it is divorce after consummation according to their principle, and another mahr by the consummation due to legal semi-connection, and he does not become a reverter because the divorce is ba'in; by the third marriage she is divorced a third time, and she gets a mahr, and another mahr by the consummation, total five and a half mahr: three mahr for three consummations, half mahr for the first marriage, and two mahr for the other two marriages. End.
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling when a man says to his wife 'Whenever I marry you, you are divorced' and then marries her multiple times in one day, consummating each time. The core principle is whether the consummation (dukhul) in the first marriage legally counts as consummation in the second marriage. According to Imam Muhammad, the first consummation does not enter the second marriage, so each marriage and consummation are independent, resulting in four and a half mahr (half mahr for each of the first two divorces before consummation, and full mahr for each consummation, with the third marriage adding one and a half). According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (called 'the two'), the first consummation counts for the second marriage, so the second marriage's divorce occurs after consummation (thus full mahr) and the second consummation is considered a return (raj'a) with no additional mahr, while the third marriage is invalid (since she is still married? Wait, the text says 'because marrying a married woman is invalid' — this is because according to them, after the second divorce ba'in, she is in 'iddah, and the third marriage in 'iddah is invalid). Thus the mahr totals five and a half: one and a half for first marriage, full mahr for second divorce, and two mahr for the two consummations. The dispute is based on the earlier ruling about 'the separated woman who remarries in her 'iddah' — Muhammad says she completes the first 'iddah (so first consummation does not count for second), while the two say she starts a fresh 'iddah (so first consummation counts). The passage also covers the case where the divorce is ba'in (irrevocable) instead of raj'i, leading to similar calculations but with the additional point that the second consummation does not effect a return because the divorce is ba'in.

Key Terms
عدة (‘iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death of husband before remarriage.
دخول (dukhul): Actual consummation of the marriage (sexual intercourse).
طلاق بائن (talaq ba’in): Irrevocable divorce where the husband cannot take back his wife without a new marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) 4.5 mahr
C) 5.5 mahr
D) 6 mahr

Key Takeaway
The difference between Imam Muhammad and the two regarding whether consummation in the first marriage counts for the second leads to a one-mahr difference in multiple marriage scenarios.

Apostasy During Iddah: Clarifying the Number of Marriages
Apostasy cases and textual correction on number of marriages

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct sequence of marriages in a case involving apostasy during iddah and identify the textual correction from Fath al-Qadir.

Core Idea
Only two marriages are needed even with apostasy; the third marriage is a copyist error.

This lesson focuses on the fifth, seventh, and eighth scenarios in the list, all of which involve a woman who is divorced ba'in, remarried during iddah, and then experiences apostasy. The author clarifies that the sequence requires only two marriages, not three, and critiques a repetition in Fath al-Qadir.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base scenario
The woman is divorced ba'in, then remarried during iddah. Afterwards, she apostatizes, returns to Islam, and is married again (or divorced before consummation).
The key is that apostasy does not create a new iddah; it only suspends it.
2
Note the author's critique
The author points out that describing a third marriage is unnecessary; the governing principle is that only two marriages occur: the first remarriage in iddah and the second after apostasy and return.
The third marriage mentioned in some texts is a mistake by copyists.
3
Understand the legal effect
Apostasy during iddah annuls the marriage, but if the woman returns to Islam before the iddah ends, the marriage is revived. Therefore, only one additional marriage contract is needed after the ba'in divorce.
This is consistent with Hanafi rulings on apostasy and iddah.
4
Apply to the eighth scenario
The eighth scenario is similar but the apostasy occurs before consummation of the second marriage. The same principle applies: only two marriages are involved.
The number of marriages is independent of the timing of apostasy relative to consummation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وطلقها بائناً ثم تزوجها في المرض في عدتها وطلقها بائناً قبل الدخول هل يكون فاراً أم لا . ورابعها لو تزوجت بغير كفء ودخل بها ففرق القاضي بينهما بطلب الولي ثم تزوجها هذا الرجل في العدة بمهر وفرق القاضي بينهما قبل أن يدخل بها كان عليه المهر الثاني كاملاً وعدة مستقبلة عندهما استحساناً، وعند محمد نصف المهر الثاني وعليها تمام العدة الأولى. وخامسها تزوجها صغيرة ودخل بها ثم طلقها بائناً ثم تزوجها في العدة ثم ارتدت والعياذ بالله تعالى ثم أسلمت فتزوجها في العدة ثم طلقها قبل الدخول؛ هكذا ذكر في فتح القدير بتكرار التزوج ثلاثاً ولا حاجة إليه في التصوير ويكفي فيه أنه تزوجها مرتين وأن الردة حصلت مرة واحدة فليتأمل وسابعها تزوجها ودخل بها ثم طلقها بائناً ثم تزوجها في العدة ثم ارتدت ثم أسلمت فتزوجها في العدة ثم طلقها قبل الدخول وثامنها تزوجها ودخل بها ثم طلقها بائناً ثم تزوجها في العدة ثم ارتدت قبل الدخول وتاسعها تزوج أمة ودخل بها ثم أعتقت فاختارت نفسها ثم تزوجها في العدة ثم طلقها قبل الدخول. وعاشرها تزوج ودخل بها ثم طلقها بائناً ثم تزوجها في العدة فأعتقت فاختارت نفسها قبل الدخول؛ كذا فتح القدير والمعراج . أمة قوله : (وخامسها تزوجها صغيرة ودخل بها ثم طلقها بائناً ثم تزوجها في العدة) يوجد في بعض النسخ بعد هذا ما نصه فبلغت فاختارت نفسها قبل الدخول . سادسها تزوج امرأة ودخل بها ثم طلقها بائناً ثم تزوجها في العدة. وفي بعضها لم يوجد ذلك بل وجد ثم ارتدت ثم أسلمت الخ. والظاهر أن ذلك إسقاط من النساخ لقوله بعده وسابعها فلا بد لها من سادسة لكن هذه السادسة المسألة السابعة بعينها فهي مكررة على أنها ليست موجودة في عبارة الفتح بل الموجود فيها غيرها ونصها وسادسها تزوجها صغيرة فلم يدخل بها فبلغت فاختارت نفسها ثم تزوجها في العدة ثم طلقها قبل الدخول انتهت وفيه أنها إذا اختارت قبل الدخول من أين تجب عليها العدة؟ ولعل المؤلف لذلك لم يذكرها. ثم رأيت في التتارخانية ما يعين أن ما في الفتح تحريف حيث قال : الثالثة تزوج صغيرة ودخل بها فبلغت الخ. فقول الفتح فلم يدخل بها صوابه ودخل بها» قوله: (ولا حاجة إليه في التصوير الخ إذا اقتصر على ما ذكره تصير عين المسألة الثامنة فتكرر وحينئذ فالسادسة
And he divorced her irrevocably, then married her during illness in her iddah and divorced her irrevocably before consummation: is he considered a fugitive or not? Fourth: If she married a non-compatible match and he consummated, then the judge separated them at the request of the guardian, then this man married her during the iddah with a dowry, and the judge separated them before consummation, then he must pay the full second dowry and a new iddah according to the two companions by istihsan, while according to Muhammad it is half the second dowry and she completes the first iddah. Fifth: He married her as a minor and consummated, then divorced her irrevocably, then married her during the iddah, then she apostatized (God forbid), then she became Muslim, then he married her during the iddah, then divorced her before consummation. Thus it is mentioned in Fath al-Qadir with repetition of marriage three times, but there is no need for it in the description; it suffices that he married her twice and that apostasy occurred once, so reflect. Seventh: He married her and consummated, then divorced her irrevocably, then married her during the iddah, then she apostatized, then became Muslim, then he married her during the iddah, then divorced her before consummation. Eighth: He married her and consummated, then divorced her irrevocably, then married her during the iddah, then she apostatized before consummation. Ninth: He married a slave woman and consummated, then she was freed and chose herself, then he married her during the iddah, then divorced her before consummation. Tenth: He married and consummated, then divorced her irrevocably, then married her during the iddah, then she was freed and chose herself before consummation. Thus in Fath al-Qadir and al-Mi'raj. Ama. He said: (And fifth: He married her as a minor and consummated, then divorced her irrevocably, then married her during the iddah) In some copies after this is the text: 'Then she reached puberty and chose herself before consummation.' Sixth: He married a woman and consummated, then divorced her irrevocably, then married her during the iddah. In some copies this is not found, but rather there is 'then she apostatized, then became Muslim etc.' Apparently this is an omission by the copyists because of his saying after it 'seventh', so she must have a sixth. But this sixth is the same as the seventh issue, so it is repetitive. However, it is not found in the wording of Fath al-Qadir, but rather something else is found there: 'And sixth: He married her as a minor and did not consummate, then she reached puberty and chose herself, then he married her during the iddah, then divorced her before consummation.' It ends. In it is that if she chooses before consummation, how would iddah be incumbent upon her? Perhaps the author did not mention it for that reason. Then I saw in al-Tatarkhaniyya what indicates that what is in Fath al-Qadir is a distortion, as he said: 'The third: He married a minor and consummated, then she reached puberty etc.' So what Fath al-Qadir said 'and he did not consummate' is correct: 'and he consummated'. He said: (There is no need for it in the description etc.) If he restricts himself to what he mentioned, it becomes exactly the eighth issue, and it is repeated. Then the sixth becomes?
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage is a continuation of a list of specific cases regarding a woman divorced irrevocably (ba'in) who remarries during her iddah period. The author presents cases involving apostasy, a minor reaching puberty and choosing herself, and a slave woman being freed and choosing herself. The commentary critically examines textual variants found in Fath al-Qadir and other works, pointing out inconsistencies and correcting the number of marriages in each scenario. The key point is that the rulings depend on the sequence of events, and the author clarifies that only two marriages are needed in some cases, not three.

Key Terms
عدة (iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death of her husband before remarrying.
بائن (ba'in): Irrevocable divorce that ends the marriage with no right of return.
ارتداد (irtidad): Apostasy from Islam, which results in annulment of marriage and affects iddah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the correct version of the fifth scenario, how many times is the woman married?
A) Three
B) Two
C) One
D) Zero

Key Takeaway
Apostasy during iddah does not increase the number of valid marriage contracts; only two marriages occur in the sequence.

Module 2 · Lesson 650

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
8 min
Emancipation and Choice in Iddah Remarriage
Cases of slave emancipation and khiyar al-bulugh during iddah remarriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the ruling when a slave wife is freed and chooses herself during iddah, then is remarried and divorced before consummation.

Core Idea
A slave wife's emancipation gives her the option to annul the marriage; subsequent remarriage in iddah is valid.

This lesson examines the ninth and tenth scenarios in the list, which involve a slave woman who is freed and then chooses herself (khiyar al-bulugh) during the iddah period. The author presents the rulings when this happens before or after remarriage and divorce.

Guided Path
1
Understand khiyar al-bulugh
A slave wife, upon emancipation, has the option to annul the marriage (khiyar al-bulugh). If she chooses herself, the marriage is annulled and iddah begins.
This option is specific to the Hanafi school.
2
Ninth scenario: emancipation before remarriage
The woman is initially a slave, married, divorced ba'in, then remarried during iddah. She is then freed and chooses herself, then divorced before consummation. The ruling: the remarriage in iddah is valid, and the divorce requires full iddah.
Her choice annuls the previous marriage but does not affect the new one.
3
Tenth scenario: emancipation after remarriage but before consummation
The woman is freed after the remarriage in iddah but before consummation, and she chooses herself. The author rules that the remarriage is still valid, and the divorce before consummation requires only half the dowry.
The timing of emancipation does not change the validity of the remarriage.

Commentary
This passage is a continuation of a list of specific cases regarding a woman divorced irrevocably (ba'in) who remarries during her iddah period. The author presents cases involving apostasy, a minor reaching puberty and choosing herself, and a slave woman being freed and choosing herself. The commentary critically examines textual variants found in Fath al-Qadir and other works, pointing out inconsistencies and correcting the number of marriages in each scenario. The key point is that the rulings depend on the sequence of events, and the author clarifies that only two marriages are needed in some cases, not three.

Key Terms
عدة (iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death of her husband before remarrying.
أمة (amah): A female slave.
اختارت نفسها (ikhtarat nafsaha): She chose herself (i.e., exercised the option to annul the marriage upon emancipation).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the tenth scenario, when the slave woman is freed after the remarriage in iddah but before consummation, what is the effect of her choosing herself?
A) The remarriage is annulled
B) The remarriage remains valid
C) The iddah is cancelled
D) The dowry is increased

Key Takeaway
A slave wife's option to annul upon emancipation does not affect a new marriage entered during iddah after the option is exercised.
